O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the last part of the art of medicine, with its explanations and its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with this manual, which is the handiwork of hands, that is to say, "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is treated in our region and is strange from all parts, it is very difficult to know and comprehend its science and scope, and there is no delay in its force except for the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed and science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	For it seems to me that I should refresh this treatise with the arrangement of this manual according to the path of explanations and declarations and abbreviations; and I will come with the forms of the ferroys of cautery, and other instruments of the work with the assistance of the declaration and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that good masters of hands are not found in our time, the art of medicine is weakened.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who deals with it must surmount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as far as he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and unions and separations of bones, and has knowledge of the nerves and joints and numbers of the fingers, and the movement and veins moving and resting, and their outlet.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the non-professional with work is little, and with his hands is less; and most of all in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that he who is not familiar with the things mentioned above should be careful not to make mistakes and not to harm people; thus I have often wanted many of those who deal with this science and who abandon themselves to theory and not to experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut open an abscess on the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries in the neck; for so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; he took out a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if they cut him open, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took in our duke's leg that was broken, and with the fracture there was a wound; and the physician, out of ignorance, cut off the fracture from the wound by means of a strong ligature, and left the wound uncovered, and finished it like this; and he commanded that it should not be unbound; and he delayed it so that the leg completely vớiered, and the bone went to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come to loosen the leg; and when I loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain at all.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	However, all roads to recovery for this member were already closed, and it could not be cured; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the members were completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder which broke out into an abscess, and then inflamed because of the evil of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is purulent because of melancholy humor, cannot be touched with iron unless it is in its right place so that one can completely cut off what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, very fine son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of these in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For as much as it is necessary for you to keep yourself safe, so that the foolish talk of others cannot harm you; If you take your weapons in concord, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that, through the grace of God, you come to salvation and are loosed; and leave behind you probable diseases of grief health; and lay aside your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to another of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Gaalien continues his treatise with the following: "Do not take on the care of a sick person, lest you be called a fool yourself.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauterizations and water-based medicinal treatments, and the subsequent chapters are ordered from the beginning to the end, including the forms of instruments, the fermness of cauterization, and everything else necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with cutting, piercing, suction cups, wounds, extracting arrows, and similar matters; it also contains instructions on the order and shapes of tools.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torments, and similar matters; it also contains instructions on the order and shapes of tools as far as cutting is concerned, and some forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work; it is necessary that I speak about the quality of aid and the harm of each kind.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the most distant word and subtle science and its responses; and many wise men would speak about it, and agree with it; and I am short of words, for I shorten the time.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that universal aid cauterizes all complexes, except for two: one is hot in nature and matter, the other dry in nature and matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, they all agreed and said that cautery is great aid; and one said the opposite: That cautery is not useful for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire if it is hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat or dryness; and he who spoke opposite said that cautery is great aid for hot and dry disease which comes in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And any way, none but he who has tried it, and who knows by long practice the nature of the cautery, and the diversity of the complexions of men, their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the effects and space of the ten; for the other complexions we have no fear, even if they are cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this should be gathered together and agreed upon to the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that the fire cautery is better for certain secretions and of greater value than the medicinal fire cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removing, and cause malady by its high heat and by the goodness of its substance; and perhaps it does not harm, unless there is too much of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And which I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the truth of things; and for that reason I excuse the length of speech, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is given to fire, and the quality of the work, how it rejects diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in proofing; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made in what season the caultures should be performed, and let them be prayed for.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all seasons, because the harm caused by what is to come can be prevented by the aid of cauterization; and most especially, if cauterization is done for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, my son, as they do, for when a disease is healed by cauterization, it never returns; and that is how it should be; but it is not like that, for cauterization is no more than medicine that changes the surface, dries up the humors that cause pain, and has more power than medicine due to its swiftness, and due to its virtue and dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l'aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n'est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And there are things that can be done so that the disease comes according to the complexion of the sick and the place of the disease and its virtue; and excesses are gathered in him by acquiring meat and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in the place where he has a little excess and moisture, as with deep cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return again; but it happens a little.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, open well, for fire cauterization is a medicine from the inside; do not follow the foolish looks of others.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Therefore, the ancient ones used to say that gold-based instruments are more efficacious than those made of iron, and they said that fire cauterization was effective only due to the quality of gold and its high purity; they also stated that the heat of the cauterization does not cause scarring, but this is not always true, as we have proven through experience, and it is true in some people; gold-based cauterization is more efficacious than iron-based, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And whenever you heat gold-based instruments, you will not be able to tell by the color of gold alone when they are hot enough, and they often cool down quickly; and if you heat them too much, they turn black in the fire, which is a sufficient impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use our fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter to the end, because the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for the head when it is moist or cold, and because of many humors that descend from the hair, and to the ears, and by a lot of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and especially because of all the diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, lameness, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a solu
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the cross between your hands, and have them grasp his pelvis; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his penis between his two roots; and if it comes to your two hands, let it bleed a little, then heat the fire called "olive" from which there is this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the mark of ink, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in turning; then let your hand fall aside, and return to the mark again, and if you do not see the bone a little, then start the fire again until you see the bone as I told you; after that, take a piece of rope, and put soft cotton inside, and put it on the mark, and leave it for three days; after that, put wet cotton inside the cloth, and let it be there until it is heated by the fire; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrarchymy", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said that when the wound is left to fester longer, it festers more; and for this reason if aid is not prompt.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should allow the cauterization to last so long that part of the bone is burned, and then resect what is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said that one should allow the cauterization to last so long and burn it so hard that the humor is pushed out of the bone by as much as a woman puts fire in her cauldron for what is needed to be expelled; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; then it must be cured and made whole.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem good to me in any way except that in some men where there is a chance of fear; and it seems to me that I should allow this; for the shoulder is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other members; and moreover, when the shoulder of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems more safe and mild to me, and of this one I use in such a way that it is salutary.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of old age pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all the head comes chronic pain, and lasts long enough, then you must use yeris and pills that are called 'cochie', and head purging and oils and ointments; and if you do the cautery that we have mentioned above, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient is of strong nature, and is not too cold; then apply the fire cautery to him as little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the fire cautery on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we said above, and made the cautery where it is called 'vesselz'; and place the cupping vessels there; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone at all: the patient feels much more severe pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about that later; and it is necessary that the cornes cauteries be thinner than those of which we made the head cautery, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	If you want to cauterize with fire, order the patient to let his hair grow long and even;
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly in one part of the head there is pain that spreads to the oil, and the head is cured with medicines, and all other cures that I have said in the division of diseases do not help: then you do cauterization according to two ways, namely with water medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	If you want to cauterize with water medicine, you squeeze a garlic clove and extract the juice from it, and then apply it to the head, keeping it there for a short time, and then you let it rest on the skin; when it has soaked into the skin, if it is dry, and you tie and tighten it well, and leave it like that for twelve hours; and then you release it and treat it with garlic juice, leaving the wound like that for two or three days; then put cotton wicks in butter to soak up the juice.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of pain as long as it is healthy; and if you see that this medicine, which I have written about in my book on burning medicines, does not work, then use another medicine that burns.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery, if done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "close" because the head is made in the form of a hole or it has I bit of a curve, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and put it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, so that half of the pain of the wound is burned; and release your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, which is done quickly, and escapes a lot of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, wet cotton with oil, and put it on the spot for three days; then dip the cotton in butter, and then treat the sore spot with pain until it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer called "cultellare", all along the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine, as we have previously said in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cauterization before mentioned with medicine and iron does not suffice, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and thus mark on the aching spot a line of half an inch long, and hold your hand back once, and strain it so that you do not cover the artery and do not come to the bone; and guard against the jaw that moves when you yawn, and let the muscle relax only as much as it needs to move, and do not let spasms come to the disease, and guard against the release of blood from the artery when it is cop
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these fire cauterizations do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him with a hot iron at the base as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said, or the extract of the artery with the cauterization that has II knives; and these fire cauterizations are better than those and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	In order to prevent pain in the ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold, and you have used the soluable medicines and other cures we spoke of in the division on ears, and the pain does not go away, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", whose form is:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying this "poins" all around the ear that hurts, or around both where the pain is felt at the base of the ear then moving away from the root of the ear, you will have X points around each ear; then heal the area until it is well.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	which must be cured by cautery is not more dangerous than those that move with fluidity, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and do not make any cauterization on the similarities that come from scalds and vomit of fish.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this similarity of torture that moves with fluidity from hydromion and purgatives of the head and gargling, and it does not matter, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, and another a little further away on the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and apply the cautery to the part that is healthy, and let the cautery burn for half of what it takes to be burned; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the appearance of the cuttlefish that we have put before you, but it is a little more delicate and it is necessary that the knives are a little larger; after treatment, set it in place as I said above, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexies are old and you treat them as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I heat up what is called a "vessel" as we have said before, and a cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	with salt
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large years and pilules of the brain; after reposing the head of the patient entirely, and putting on it, at the nape, the plaster of saffron, which is written or said to be made into plasters; and this is the way of cauterizing: do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy then it is good; and if it is not, three fire cauterizations should be made to the scalp from the base of the neck down, with two inches between each cauterization; and the treatment should continue as with the others, until the hair begins to grow again; but if there are signs that the hair will not grow again, one cauterization should be made in the middle, and two others on either side of the head; and the treatment should continue until the scalp is healed; and let the cauterizations which are called "olives" be performed as I have said above.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold at the top
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the scalp be cleansed from the front and back and from the sides, as we have said above; after this, the scalp of the patient should be treated with fire cauterizations, one on top and another on each side, and one behind and three at the base of the neck; and if there is more need, and the hair is wet and the patient suffers, and the patient is worse, then three cauterizations should be made at the back of the head; and leave it until the fire has burned the most recent scar, and lift your hand; after this, treat the scalp until it is healed, and let the cauterizations which are called "olives" be performed as we have said above.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For the epileptic person, fire cautery should only be used for those who are fleumatic, and first the brain must be cleansed and other treatments must be given as we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from penance.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot endure the punishment, then make gargarisms and chewing to cleanse the brain frequently with bonecies; after that, place the head in the middle and apply the fire as we have said above, and also on the neck and back of the spine, and apply the fire olive-wise as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, then make the fire cautery in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excess fluids or腐爛腐爛的濕潤物， then half-burn half-curse as we have said to the one who has paralysis。
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy is the excess of decline to melancholy, and the body of the sick is moistened， then he does something to drink so that the brain is purified， according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After remove the head of the sick; after make a turban well made, as well as a circle, if put it under the head; and let the sick lie in good position from all sides; then present the liniment, and anoint with old beeswax; and heat it slightly with fire so that he can bear it; after empty the circle inside under the head, and let it cool off; and make this to the sick every week once with other good government， until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if he pricks at his base, then hold him steady so that he does not move until they grow.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	For this way of cauterizing makes the skull smooth and even; and then put cotton dipped in water on it, and in grease of lamb.
de l’awe des eulz	of the hair
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awed comes first by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do this to the patient purifying thing, and warding away all moisture, and making him sweat or bathe many times while fast.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Then instruct him to rub his head again, and make a fire cautery on the head, and make II cauteries on the temples because they are both dislocated from awed and both together, or one is dislocated and one is not; and wrap all the cauterized places with linen bandages, and ward off any blood loss, and if too much blood comes out, then stop it by tying it up tightly as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in cauterization how to stop it; and never is cauterization done or stopped with heat from behind the two bones.
dou cors des larmes	the eyes of tears

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the eyes of tears within the eyes

de coi ci est li forme:	from this is the form:

dou poil qui point l’oil	hair that holds oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Now the hair that holds the oil has come to the doctor's office, and it grabs the oil, and he makes two types of fire: that is, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the figure that you have signed little by little several times, so that the burns are in place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up at the touch of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for III days, then put cotton soaked in oil in a poultice until the scorching is over; after the wound has been dressed until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hair comes back, and the paper is softened then start again with the cautery on the same place as before, and if the hair is gone, then cauterize until the paper returns to its natural position, and remains even, and does not touch the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical treatise suggests that the patient should be instructed to let the hair grow long and even, then make a parchment into the shape of an olive leaf; then take French soap and warm water, each 1 oz., and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it doesn't cool down, then, as you have made the shape of an olive leaf, put it on the paper; and if the disease is in one place only, then apply it there, and also in both places; and soak the cotton with oil, and the patient's foot should be in your hand, and put two drops of the medicine on it every time the patient feels tingling from the medicine, because he feels tingling as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	If you have had this for a long time, keep the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the cauterization is over, raise up the lid of the mouth, and let it be raised as if it had been raised by fire or by cutting; and if so, that's good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, make sure that your wound is not affected by the medicine's eyes.
