Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size, and according to this one is bound; and is not answered the straight way to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistulas as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is appropriate that you make a cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dry the hair with a towel or with persil juice on oil; then heat the cauterizer, and when it is hot, touch it to the hair at the root, keeping it there until it burns; if you see, so point it from one hair to another, and if you do not see, so touch it as a tent; but all the same, this that is burned should be for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Apres press the fistula shall be opened, and there treat it with perspiration and drying; and if it is closed, then operate, and try firmly the bow; after put on the cauterizer so that your hand is not at fault; and place the cauterizer in the grease of the oil, and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the cauterization just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cauterization again, and if you need more, let it rest for III days; after put on cotton wet in grease, and cure with drying medicine until it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is not healthy, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and treat according to what came out in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way to cauterize a fistula, which no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Do you understand about a fistula, and pierce the place; after that put in the fine needle so as it is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I make it in the quantity of a .Z. of drop; and hold your hand firm whereon the needle is, so that the drops fall not away, but you put the oil to the cotton wet in water or vinegar: the drop, if artfully put at the place of the fistula, and healed per marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the fire that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if not, then you should give a push to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the bridge of the nose according to what it is fitting in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	creases in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Mouth times have creases in the lips that are called "hair", and sometimes in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these creases as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not profit, then apply a small surgical cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it in the creases as long as it comes out clear; after, clean it with oil until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after having made pus and it is dry and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, but it does not profit: then you must take a cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after, you plug or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes out at the bottom of it, and do so once or twice, after treating as we have said in the treatment, as long as it is healthy; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, then you must discover the place and cut off the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, but this does not work, then put the chief of the illness in your mouth; after that heat the cautery so that its form comes out in a certain way as you put a chain on the tooth; and put the cautery hot inside, and hold for so long as the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then let go your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; after that fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and wash it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the teeth that were moving are fixed, the gums that were softened are tightened, and the moisture that has corrupted it is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, either in the cold or the heat, and medicines do not help, then there is a need for two types of cauterization: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter if it is such that you squeeze butter from a cheesecloth, and the tip into a teaspoon of iron or bronze; then take cotton and wrap it over the tip of a tent, and moisten it with butter and place it on the tooth tenderly and keep it as long as it cools down; and do this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the cotton and the wool are moistened with butter and placed on the tooth tenderly, and put on a piece of iron hot enough for the fire to come to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire if it is such that you squeeze a piece of iron or bronze wire, and make it thick enough so that the fire does not come into the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, for it will form a blister afterward, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be increased the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then he should swallow it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery of the tooth that you will, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	from scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of cold moisture and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the head of the cane so that there comes what form, and has II openings for the fumes to come out on the cane from the other side; and put the cane hot on the abscess once, or where it is necessary, as long as it comes to the root of the abscess; and let the abscess be small if you put cane according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for III days; and put cotton wet with butter on it as long as the burning is over; then cure the wound of ointments and tents until it is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails on the cheeks and most especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should be voided first by laxative medicines; afterwards, apply cauterization to the root of the throat, and you must not go up to the throat, and do not dare to use a cure except with water.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, apply another cauterization to the joint of the neck at the base of the spine, and the cauterization which is called 'clavicle', so that we have the shape in front; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of the mouth are caused by cold moisture, and the patient does not have a fever or any pain, and the disease is old, then apply two cauterizations to the lip at the edges; and another cauterization goes up between the nipples; and the cauterization which is called 'clavicle' according to the shape that is in front.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make the fire cautery by poking all the cauterizes called "poins" that are before in the disease of the ears; and let the pokes be until XXX, or more.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the wound according to what has been said before, and let the cauterizes be of three rains according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those where the cautery is lighter, for those that you make III in a row.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, be gentle on the patient on his back and on his ribcage; afterwards, lift up what is inside the little hole with your right hand; and if the joint moves inside, then heat the cautery that has two holes here according to this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize it as long as he pierces up to the cost, and comes out with the figure of the cautery all together IIII cauteries; and for this is made cauterization with the cautery that has III ners, because the figure of the cauterization are there cauteries; and they are the nervi according to the subtility of a tent and this is the form of the cautery that has III ners:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is placed on this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After putting the fire on the skin to burn it slightly with a hook; after that let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, such a thing happens, then do a cauterization on the thick part of the cautery with an edge, or more cauterizations in puncturing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed up, and the moisture is dried up from it, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach there come chills and moisture until he was removed from his complexion, and are multiplied the catarrh to him, and the customs of treatment accustomed, and does not profit, so it is necessary that the patient be covered with a blanket, and spread his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From then after him do three cauteries with the milk of the pis for the quantity of a double, to all the cauterizes clavile, and two cauteries defuers on the two sides as much as the shape of the cauterizes is at three angles, and have space between the one and another that they are not joined together when they go with the fire; and be the cautery so perfect that it scorches the two parts of the wound, and is the shape of the cauterizes according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you cauterize with a large cauldron the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cauldron, cauterize by piercing and signing on the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize all the cauldron which is called "pinch".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure for the cure that we have had before, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, it comes with pain from cold and moisture and strong windiness, as long as it is too full of its natural composition due to excesses; and the patient is cured of what we have said in the divisions, and it does him no good, unless he is cautious about his diet; and mark three cauterizes according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, far away from each other, the thickness of two fingers; and let the cauldron be long on the chest, and do not press very hard on all the cauldron; and let it be burned with such heat that half of it is burned, and let the patient lie down on his back; and if he cannot, then let him stretch out his legs, and lift his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauterizes of the cutlet, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn up all the flesh, for you would make the whole body dry; and let it come only to the eyelid, because the cure is very subtle in place, and the sight to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you can tell whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the parenchyma, then the patient feels pain that is not too great; and if it is in the capsule, then the pain is very intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure has ended the pus, let the patient be quiet on his head; and then sign with your hand where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that is like a raisin, so as to get the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cautery until the curings be burned, and come as far as the swelling, so that the whole porridge be burnt; after the cure according to the cure of poultices until it is sound; and it only concerns that this cautery use no fire but they who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by which hands these diseases have been corrupted on any occasion.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then it may be able to work firmly, and always I seem that he moves less.
dou cautere de pleuresin	and for the pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and for the pleurisy The old people used to say that one should make plagues of root of aristoloche, and in this way: take a root of aristoloche long, the largest that you can find, dry it, and also make it as thick and as long as your two hands; then moisten it with oil, and heat it on the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the clavicle and the collarbone, and I small cauterizes a little down in the part that is sore by the beard; and cauterize II between the fifth rib and the sixth, turning back a little; and let me suck the milk, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and another between two shoulders after the milk has passed; and do not press your hand, otherwise make it open as if you are smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no one of the ancients said that any man use fire cautery resembling a razor, and he blows it and puts it between the ribs until it comes to the apoplectic seizure; and he leaps out of pain, as we have said in the apoplexy of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse with any of the three ways we have spoken about, and it does not benefit, then they put three kinds of fire cautery, all of which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one way is this: you make three cauterizations, or four, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the fire cautery for the liver that we have spoken about before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient sneeze behind him; and another way of cauterizing is this: you heat the cautery which has two roots, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and bring the burn which is in place of the mouse, or the knife's edge comes from the left, and are the elevations where you bring the burn according to the burn, according to the length of the back, and the cautery is according to the breadth of the back.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After putting the two flames so that their heat is felt on both sides, and then applying the fire cautery, and so on for four times; if you see, then cauterize all of it with three flames.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure has been exposed to the air for a long time, and this is what we have experienced that the other cure in front of it said.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Do not cauterize with the method called "asclepiades".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you have performed the cure according to the ways that we have mentioned in the divisions, and your cure does not profit, then it is necessary that you do four cauterizations around the navel, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the kidneys, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place the pyre.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the fire cautery to go away pus long time, and do not leave the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would be quick, and both intentions will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the fire cautery for the abdomen is like a key that we have in front of us; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is described in front.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the joints swell up in those who are hydropic and are pale yellow in color, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the index and middle fingers; and gently remove your hand from the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deep, otherwise the pale yellow would come out, and let the cauterization be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the scrotum; let the cauterization be long, one behind the knee and the other in front, between the leg; and leave the cauterizations for a long time without treating, that they burn themselves; after which treat the others as we have said.
de la menoison	of the hospital
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtues that retain and digest it are present in the stomach and in the intestines are affec ted, and cannot be treated by any means of treatment; and you see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, so do I make a large cauterization on the stomach according to what he has spoken before or a cauterization of the stomach, circulating; and four cauterizations around the navel finely to all the cauterizations that are clavels, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a fire cautery on his hand, and make each finger a cautery, and two small cauteries in his stomach to relieve the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	for the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the root, or one or more, and they are old and there are big cold and moist corrupting humors, and they are cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit if fire cauterizations are made: three on the spine of the back, that which is all farther from the anus, little by little and triangularly, and one cauterization above the two; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and meat doesn't cook there, and the face swells, then leave the cauterization open for a long time.

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the callus which is called "thelula

When you chop off the callus, if it gets hot, heat the cauldron which seems like a razor, and then let it burn completely over the chopped callus; and leave it for as long as your hand can stand it, so that the cauterization comes to the birth of the vein, from which it is cut; do this once or twice, and if there is much of a callus, cauterize each one as we have said; after the use of beneficial ointments as long as they are healthy; and if you cauterize with a large cauldron on the chin, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a bad wound

When the patient cannot bear to have it cut or opened, we will tell you in your place, that there comes a disease which cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no opening of the vein, and it is inflamed and wet with pus and corruption, then you must provide the whole tent with a delicate substance, and be sure that you know exactly how much of the tent it is.

se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula runs through the belly and intestine, be careful of these veins, and do not pierce them except in the flesh, and believe that they are not dangerous; after healing the vein as long as it is healthy, and if the veins have been cut, and the bone has been exposed for a long time, then know that the vein is completely healed; and if the bones have not been exposed, know that the veins have been split, and the bone has corroded at the bottom; and so, as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	from the wound

de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac. de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip

When the pain comes in the hip joint, and it is caused by cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated as we have described in the dislocation, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient with large pills of foul-smelling pills, or other bad-looking pills.

Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction. Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere. Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When there is pain in the joints due to moisture that spreads to each limb, and when the pain comes from a cold cause and cannot be cured with medicines, then cure it with fire in this way: make the fire cautery between the joints of the foot, and let the fire cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to hold on the face of the foot, make cautery all the way down with "no point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, make cautery on each knee III cauteries or IIII of each part, with olive cauterization; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand firm except for as long as the skin of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, administer the cauterization that we have spoken about in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, do a single line of cauterization; and if there is still pain in two joints and in the hair of the hand, cauterize each joint and the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and govern the patient well and give him medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do this good government and you purge the pus, then you will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syrup
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the balls descend as coins and it is newly, then it is necessary that when you look at him curiously, he does not vomit; and uses things that leave his belly, so that the end descends from his belly; after he sits down on his back between your hands, and orders him to wet his beard as long as the balls are repaired, and take them in your hands, and sign from the bottom of the rupture on the bone of the finger, and everything has a form like half a circle above the chest; then heat the fire with this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it drips dry.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then let the balls come back to their place; and let the assistant wet his hand so that he does not turn back; and well work on the legs of the patient, and put a cloth and a servant on the legs, and another one under the feet that wet his hands; then put the fire cautery on his limb until your entire hand reaches the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again several times until you come to the bone; and be careful so that the ball does not slide when you make the cauterization; that you do not burn him; and that by this disease the patient does not die, or another misfortune.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you reach the bone with the fire cautery, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and of adults also great ones according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cauterization with a burse until the scorching is done; after this cure other remedies until he is well, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well fixed; and it is necessary that these treatments be prolonged, so that the ball does not slide when he tries to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is given to him, and it is applied for another forty days; and he has good rest, that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and too much noise; and when he follows this teaching, he completely recovers.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of the tailor in his paste.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, make the cauterization of the third cure according to what we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it must be cauterized at the cautery's three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the area of the incision and make a line across its width, and another below it, and with your hand press down on all the cauterized cloven.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, or from sitting or being hurt, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medicine cure does not help, then it is appropriate that he be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poyn", and be cauterized according to the length of the member, and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location from torments and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed with the first cauterization, that is good; but if not, then begin another cauterization on top of that one, for this custom is that it must move to the member that is closest, so that you must make the cauterizations as long as the patient remains unhealed.
de meselerie	of relaxation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The meseile are helped not at all by the cautery with great help, and most often the disease that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see that the fire cautery is causing the patient discomfort, then apply a cold compress to soothe the pain. To do this, wrap the compress around the patient's hand and leave it there until the heat subsides; then remove the compress slowly so as not to cause further distress. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et si le patient est très malade, il faut lui faire des cautères avec du feu, comme nous l'avons dit plus haut, et des cautères sur la moelle épinière du cou, et six cautères sur la moelle épinière du dos, et un grand cautère sur la nuque, et un autre petit sur le cœur, et deux petits cautères sur les épaules, et deux sur les côtes, et un sur chaque joint de main et de pied, et un sur la membrane qui recouvre l'estomac. Il faut également surveiller attentivement les nerfs qui se trouvent derrière l'épaule, pour ne pas les brûler, et ne jamais faire de cautère sur l'os du poignet ou sur celui de l'estomac, ni sur le foie.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And if the patient is very sick, you must make fire cauters as we have said above, and cauters on the spinal cord at the back of the neck, and six cauters on the spinal cord at the back, and one large cauter on the back of the neck, and one small one on the heart, and two small ones on the shoulders, and two on the ribs, and one on each joint of hand and foot, and one on the membrane that covers the stomach. You must also carefully watch the nerves behind the shoulder so as not to burn them, and never make a cauter on the wrist bone or on the stomach bone, nor on the liver. Know that when you do more cauters, the help is greater and the benefit is greater; know also that the patient does not feel pain at the cauterization as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing the head of flour with honey and other cures as long as it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling comes in any member and is cured with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healthy, then make cauterization on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little inside the cure of the ointments as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is it made cauterization and by hand and at the foot and back, to the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is osteochondritis; and nevertheless it does not matter if there are no people who know the members and outlets of moving the neck.
de albaras	of albars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the "albaras" disease is awakened and the medicine's art does not work, then cauterize it with a fire cautery that is perfect in proportion to the amount of the medicine, until the pale color is raised and changed; then cure it with flour of oats and lentils, mixed with oil of roses and leaves of plantain, and blood of lambs and of plovers, each part separately; and then mix them together and bind them with a cloth and apply them to the affected area until they are healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for leprosy by fire cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When leprosy comes at the beginning and you notice it, if you cauterize it with a fire cautery that seems like a circle all around the leprous spot.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet some say that you should also make a fire cauterization in the middle of the leprous spot; and yet I do not think this is good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it work this way; and the most correct thing is that it be cauterized all around, with the fire cautery called "circle," as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays dying or because of the excess fluid that it causes or because of the age of the sick person when he is very old and has little blood, or because of the heat; then you see him hurry to die: so cauterize him with small cauterization stings by poking; then leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see him pierce all the cauterization, so hot is the cauterization of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	and put your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has pierced the blood, and let such cauterizations that the sick person feels them in a certain way that the course of the corruption is taken away.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, as long as he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease which is called “corrodens”, and is nothing else than a festering of the member, for it eats away the members as fire dries up the wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can be treated with fire, then heat the clavers small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the disease is; after cauterizing on all sides until it is completely healed, and nothing remains of it, so that whatever is corrupted is taken away by osmosis.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it rest for three days, and put on the cauterized places oil to soothe them, so that the burns of fire are healed, and all corruption is taken away.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of those born with a bent nose.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days a healthy child is not born, it is good; and if not, begin the cauterization on that which is delayed in its place rotten.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ointment has never been cured with medicine from the fire in place of fire cauterization; but fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for the medicine from the section on dislocation: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of radishes that come to the tips
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Sometimes, because of the weather, there is a disease that is called "close" according to our intention, and it is a large, hairy thing that bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease is according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is such that you heat the cauterizer like a pen of a vault, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can poke the nail from all sides, and it has subtle edges; then you put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it comes out at the base; and let it sit like this for III days until it begins to move rust; then make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on all night, and let the nails come out and will be rooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound by charring it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the heart is turned away by defying, and many times avenges and hurts, so that it is necessary that you bring fire water cautery; and in this way: take a piece of iron or steel, or a pen of a vault, and put on the nail and the adder, that is to say, poke verrucae; and put the piece on it that it may burn all around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the piece comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water route deep until the root; and let the patient feel a little of the heat of the water for an hour; then let it be, and it will be rooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Make another after this, as long as you take out all those who are in the heart, then cure the diseases that cause fever.
li cure dou trembler	He will cure the shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake from cold, or from quartan fever or other, it is necessary that you make them four or five fire-cauterions along the spine, one cauterization between each spine; and a cauterization at the feet, and one on the stomach with olive cauterizing powder; this will stop their shaking, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No one appears on the body by way of sweat, or pus-filled blisters, that come from rotten matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary for the first time that they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the blister: a thin fire-cauterizing twig of thyme, so that its tip burns in the fire, or a long root of aristea, or a cauterizing lens.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never do the cauterize from the beginning when it appears according to this manner, and they cannot grow hair before, but breaks off the surplus thereof, and are healed; but it is necessary that this should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery has been cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great changes in the blood of the artery that has been cut off at the wound, or incised on an abscess, or cauterized on the member, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop up.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And wherever it is necessary, when you have a second finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it so much that the blood stops from gushing out of your second finger, and no more drops are left; then take some olive oil, large or small, according to the size of the wound and its location, and put all of it on fire; then take II, or a great or a small one, according to the size of the wound and its place, and hold the hot oil over the vein where you are holding your finger, and keep the oil hot as long as the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you jump too much while he is holding your arm, and the cauterization is still hot, take another piece of the cautery that is in the fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other as long as the blood has stopped flowing; and guard against burning the nerve that is delicate, and so that no other evil comes upon the sick person; and know that when the artery is cut short of the three [major] arteries, it cannot be stopped well even if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by firmly tying a thread, or by medicines put on it which have the power to stop the flow of blood; and let it be bound and stretched firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a tight binding with cloth or place burning things on it, or similar things, if it does not help, then do not do it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Et si ce arrive à aucun qu'il n'ait mie mire ni medicine présent, si doit mettre son doi indice sur la plaie de la voinne si com nous avons dit, et bien énerger tant qu'il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer l'ou doit, mais l'ou moille d'awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of remedies for diseases and injuries.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first book all about diseases that require fire, or burning medicine, and the scoops and causes and instruments and forms of the cauterizations; and I have placed this chapter from the lower part of the head to the top, and I will go now in this chapter by this same path for those who suffer more easily than those who seek treatment.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I have begun to speak of this, it is necessary, o dear one, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of the cauterize, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not venture into folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in the ways of people come to cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have so become ill with their disease that they die easily because of the confusion that arises from their illness, and from the great severity of their illness, then one must fear them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these I give you sense, and say: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is pitiable.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you grant these who come to you who have this manner, but put more great kindness in your honor than in your covetise, and do not open foolishly but carefully from the one of whom you are certain, and of whom you could possibly take and lose; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your sick so that health may be turned; and he who will help to have good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and justice, and may you will desire the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in devising by chapters, according to that which is before or cautery of the caustic, that I have devised for you from the top as far as the foot, so that you can easily find that of which you will have need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d’aigue
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	I know that this disease often occurs in children when the baby's cry is too loud and suddenly stops; and there is no reason for it to recover.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children; and of those that I have seen, many have died; and it seems to me that I should be more cautious in treating them.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was swollen with water, and the head of the child sank every day until it could not support itself; and the moisture was so great that he believed that he would die, and this moisture gathered around the bone on the side of the neck, between the collarbone and the bone; and the work is such that if you cut a large slit in the head with a knife, as far as we saw, until the moisture runs; and look at the shape of the spine:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is more moisture, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture is breaking the bone and you see the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out strongly when you press it with your hand, and it does not close again: then you should make three incisions in the following manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, remove the bandages and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and give the patient dry meat to eat so that the member heals and is healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess is, and where the angle of the aiguille [sic] is; for it is never before, never behind, never on the right, and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess opens, and the angle of the aiguille [sic], and make the incision according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and come away with blood, so that the patient dies from the pain of the blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	(regarding) the removal of the arrow, or of any other thing that is lodged in the flesh, and that causes pain;
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	(regarding) the removal of an arrow, or any other thing that is lodged in the flesh, and causes pain; When there is a disease called "cataract" (or) a pimple, and the illness is old, and medicine does not benefit, then the second cure is to make a cauterization with what you will cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Il covient donc, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d'un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l'une et de l'autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d'enche, puis cope l'une et l'autre d'un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc'a l'os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	It is necessary, then, when you cover the eyes, that the patient should put his hand behind his head; after he rubs the place with a hard cloth until the arteries appear, then pulls his neck forward completely; then look where the vein bites, and the lines of both sides are after the ears, and they have been folded; then sign the lines of the cheek, then cover both with a spatulum sharp on two sides, until the incision comes up to the bone, and this is done by the wide part of the head.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if it bleeds constantly without ceasing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign off and cut to the bone; and that which is to be put out of blood should be six inches, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone no pain, then draw the wound and bandage it, and the cure of the ointment as long as it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of grinding.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old grind comes, and catarrh is acquired, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and old dry skin and similar things, and it is medicated by methods of medical treatment and all that does not benefit it, then we draw the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
