Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If there is no pain, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is no space in the bone above, for the instrument does not come to cut: therefore you must put a piece of linen thread, not too thick, on his nose, with your fingers wrapped around each end with some space between them or less; and place the child's mouth around the thread at his power, and pull it in smelling until it comes out through his nose into his mouth; and many times do this to the child in school, and it is a light thing for him who does it; then hold the tip that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other tip that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other with your fingers wrapped around our hands where the thread is.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it as long as you know that the new wine has corrupted the must, then treat the grape, wash the blood, and moisten the grape with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the neck there right away; make it for III days or more, as long as the ointments corrode all who are delayed from drinking; and then put a plug of plaster in the neck some days while he is well, and if it has need of medicines dried, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purge the head, by which one distills the oils and medicines through the neck:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be of silver or of gold, resembling a lamp open, like a plug, and conduct it also; and if you see, make a closed plug, and be the instrument plain to purge the head; and I have many times at the head for him to keep it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the horse above the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the top of the neck there is a disease that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large so that it can be seen with the eye; and for this it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and burn the bone completely, then put fire on it; and if you delay to cover it up until it is large, if it is hard, of a pale color, poor sense: but do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when it is covered there comes great evil to the patient; and the abscess is touched gently, not with a pale color, and you see that it can be completely covered, if the patient is empty and covers it without fear, and treats the top with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the baby is born, cut and clean
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Understand that when there is a rupture in one of these joints that has been inflamed, it does little good, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when there is a rupture in one of these joints that has been inflamed, it does little good, except for some men. It is necessary, therefore, to cut and clean [the joint], and to look at the wound; then, with two sharp blades, join them together again, and then bandage it well so that it heals; and if the blades are severed on one side or the other, you must peel all the parts of the flesh until they heal, and then join the two blades again, and bind them up, and dust the powder with dragon's blood, and burn incense over it. And put a piece of plaster made from strong blood or another plaster that is available, and leave it in place until it drops by itself; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch a wound so that you gather the solution together: or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, with your hands, inside the lips, there are hard lumps like grain, small and large ones; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut each one individually, and tie them tightly and cut them into parts; then employ the vinegar of vitriol, keeping it in place until the sores are healed; and then let it be dried out, and cure the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the tooth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is a sore on the gums that the old man calls "albulus"; if it is necessary to hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, and let the blood run; then apply vinegar of vitriol or other drying and binding powders; and if this sore returns after the incision, and many times it happens, cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not return again after the cauterization, and these are the forms of the instruments to plug.
des sordens	of the orders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Of the orders: No order should be placed in the mouth between the teeth, those that are ugly and rough; and no order should the tooth be black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is stinking; so it is necessary that you place the sick between your hands, and his roots are under your hand, and pull out the teeth where they appear, without any delay; and in this way do white and yellow, and black and other colors, until they are all gone; and if one of them is at the first rasion, it is good; if not, then begin again on the second day and third, until you have all pulled out; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments to be pulled out, according to what the work demonstrates, because the puller who pulls out the teeth with others has shapes different from those who pulls between the teeth; and these shapes should be ready for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that you treat the toothache as quickly as possible, because there must be no excuse for not doing so; indeed, it is a substance that must be extracted immediately.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And then, when the patient is in pain, you must be certain about the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and he believes that it is in a healthy tooth, and has it extracted; nevertheless, the pain remains for this reason, as we have already seen with these gentlemen; and when you are certain about the toothache, you must scrape the tooth under the tooth with a sharp instrument so that the gum is completely removed from all sides; then, you place it in your hands or small pliers at one point and another, until it is well loosened, then you tighten the pliers; and let the jaw of the patient be firmly between your knees, and keep it still.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not fall, take any of these instruments and put it inside each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is stuck and won't come out, then you must fill it with threads where it gets stuck; and if it is pulled carefully with pliers, so that it doesn't break while being pulled; and you must cut the gum very cleanly around the tooth to pull it out.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must take care that you don't break it, and if some of it remains, and returns to the patient with greater pain from the root than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must take care that you don't do like that ignorant surgeon who, because of his haste and arrogance, breaks the jaw many times, and doesn't know what we have told; but rather brings about by the question of that great disease for the roots that they delay, or for the jaw that they break, as we often wanted; and when the tooth is pulled, if you wash the hole with wine or hydromel or salt; and they run away without stopping, so often happens, put the hole with vitriol broth; and if this doesn't work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that the first tooth does not mute, are to be long and thick in diameter, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when you pull it, and let them be made of good iron, and let them be sharpened to keep them in place.
de la racine des dens	the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root moves when pulled, then you must place cotton wet with oil on the place or with butter for one day.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the roots are smooth, for then the pliers that are called 'algefri' do not hurt the head; and let them be made inside like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, then you must take off the charm entirely around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'althali', that is to say a file, and this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be it flat and thick so that he does not break, and the root jumps from this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the tools, from which the shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has II rain, so that here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front in the rasion of the teeth, and this instrument which seems a pair of pliers, whose form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be so that he cannot break it, and know that many tools of teeth are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the master wise men themselves try out their tools according to what their work and the disease show them, because there are many diseases where the old do not teach tools for the diversity of them; and if he does not break the cart or other bones, on which it will lie, if you look for the tools that suit it, which I have told you, and help with gestures, so that here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return it to its place with suitable medicines for this person, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then remove all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not fit well according to the natural shape of the jaw, and the form is ugly, especially in young women, you must know that the root is not in its place, and it cannot be sewn or filed; then file it; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and which is made of iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits and tightens day by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file such as this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the lode where we make needles; and in one's hand, little by little, lightly, so that it does not move until it chimes; then, at the end, completely shaves off any razor, and its edge is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen...
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen, whether by pounding or chewing, and the patient cannot press upon what he chews so that he does not chime, and you have treated them with restringent medicines, then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and pusy, but the gold thread never moves; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you notice any gaps, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then insert the nails between the teeth, one or more, as far as you can cleanly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start again at the part where you started, and gently and carefully tighten your hand until it no longer moves; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then attach the head of the shoulder to a pair of pliers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy tooth and fasten them so that they do not injure the tongue; and then leave them in this tight position as long as it can be held, and if they slip, or the threads come loose, hold them together with another thread, if it does not break; it will last all its time, and this is the shape of the jaw and the form of the attachment of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then, if the tooth has fallen out, replace it in its place, little by little, as we have said; and let no one touch it who is not skilled and patient, and never make the shape of a tooth out of ivory, and put it back in its place where it has fallen out, and hold it fast as we have said, and let it remain in this tight position for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the liens of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is lost the lines of the tongue or nature, which are not as such; or by accident of a sore swelling; and the ovraiges are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your lap, and let go of the tongue; then copper the nerves of the lip, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or not, and it is by a sudden sore, then bite with your knife and copper the lip wide; and guard that the cut is not too perfect, for the artery that is in; and when you have done this, then lift up the water of rose and thus, or cold water, then put on the tongue a piece of linen; and dip it each night, so that the leech does not stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood rushes out, then sprinkle vinegar on top; and if it does not go away, then cauterize it with the slow cautery, which is good for that; then treat it with other treatments until it is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a red or black or hard color there, then the patient should not feel it, then do not touch it, for that is a ulcer; and if it declines towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then pour the vinegar on it, and make it with a thin blade, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it rushes out to your ovraige, then sprinkle vinegar on top until it is yellowed, then return to your ovraige as you pull all of it; then remove its head thus and that rope, and treat it with other treatments until it is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No voice comes from inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, take care: if it is an abscess of small size and light color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron either for fear of causing pain; but let it be as long as it is still alive, and then take it off, or else it will burst itself; and if it is a white color, and the root is thin, you should prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see whether the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the sick person in front of the sun, and let his shoulders be well heated, and he opens his mouth and puts his tongue between his hands, and presses the instrument against it, from which comes the form; and let it be made of silver or gold as thin as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you have pressed the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the scalpel and put it in amber, and carry it higher than you can; and do not bring anything with it, except for the handle of the instrument, from which comes the shape, which seems a few pieces; and yet their heads are coroved and they are one above another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or an iron bar.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you hold it with pliers, from which comes the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be it cut on one side and not on the other; and when you have chopped one of the ambers, then chop the other according to the same way, and after the incision gargarise the patient with hot water, and very easily, and if the blood comes out, gargarise the patient with wine or cooked pomegranates or leaves of mirth, and similar things, until the wound is healed; and never let other abscesses appear in the throat than the two ambers, if they are cut in the same way as the two ambers.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, which is to say a small-sized abscess; and I had it well sealed up all around so that the woman could not breathe through the opening that had been stopped up, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had delayed even one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been there for two rain cycles through the two openings where the nails are.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted an osprey into one of the two openings where the nails are, then went inside, and there I found a large portion of the bowels; then I refilled it in the other opening where the nails are, and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the osprey into the abscesses, and poured some of the contents out, and at that moment the opening in her throat began to open again, and she started to drink clear water and then wine, and didn't stop cutting off part of the abscess by long stretches; and the abscess receded again, and filled up the space that I had emptied out, until it grew very large; then I sewed it up and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stayed stopped up; and I left those parts behind, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the wound comes from the eye, and it is deep and far away, it is called "transverse"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eyelid".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the wound does not benefit from the treatment, and you see that the lower lid is calm and thin, then you should chop it off; and if it is round and assembled and not too far away; and it is bloody or of a dark color or black, then you must avoid the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the lazy eye.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, of its blueness and remoteness, let the patient sit in front of the sun, and press its tongue onto the instrument of which we have spoken above; then cut off the corner with a sharp knife, and take out the bullet with two tools that I mentioned in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; because if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use of what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use fire cautery on him.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then he presses the tongue of the instrument which we have said or fire cautery, and grinds with sharp water so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and by the employment of this tool's shape, from which this form comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the head have a hair where one puts the medicine, as with a spoon, and put the instrument which we have said or fire cautery on all the medicine on the nose; and let the patient lie on his side, so that he salivate and the water runs from his mouth into the medicine, if not going down his throat, and let him burn; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the nose, the quantity of half a hour, until you see it get dark and the medicine's bites are gone; and if you need to recommence the fire cautery, do so, and after the cautery rinse it with cold water, and clean what is around with a cotton bud dipped in the medicine; and let it be arised with cold water, and cure by gargling until he is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, except for the cauterization. If it is cured with this method of fumigation, take a plant and aniseed and oregano and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all together or any of them in a pot, and pour it easily and boil it; and the pot should be very tightly covered with strong earth, and place the instrument over it according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It should be of silver or gold, and let one of the bottles be put in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises through the canal to the eye until the eye is dead; then begin again often, until the eye dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of the abscess, for many things have happened; and do not do this except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog's tooth and put it in the patient's mouth so that his mouth does not become too hot; for the dog's tooth does not produce too much vapour in the mouth, and this is good treatment together with healing salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often there is an aeration in the throat of fish or nothing; so that you must take what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see movement in the thing; and if it does not open by itself and is put back into the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will be ejected by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and you tie the sponge to it, and then swallow it; and when it arrives at the place, if it moves, and then pull hard; and if it does not come out by that which we have said, then take an instrument of plunger according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.
de la sansue de la gorge	Et soit l'instrument courbé à la tête de manière qu'il puisse entrer plus facilement dans la gorge, et que la tête soit levée en haut; et garde que tu ne touches pas à l'épiglotte, que les sons ne lui viennent pas, ni ne poussez pas l'os à l'intérieur; et vaut mieux que le patient boive l'instrument, pour que s'il avale, il avale tout l'instrument en même temps.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	De la sansue de la gorge,
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, if it is all small nails, or tiny claws that reach this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if he doesn't deserve it, take a dog's tooth, and pour it down the throat of the patient, then pour or twist the tooth with fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is infected with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full jar of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in to swallow, and move it with his hand often; and if soon as the pus feels the water, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't spit as we have said, then inhale the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the incense burning process; do this many times, for it will not be able to hold back.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d'un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l'estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n'en isse mie, mais viegne jusc'a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s'elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d'aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu'elle isse fuer par cest governement.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is such that one can treat the tongue, if one can see it, as resembling pliers twisted to enter the mouth; and it has a shape like a scalpel, and it has sharpness from lime, so that whatever it takes hold of, it does not let go; and thus is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the capitis of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The heads of abscesses are, according to this memory which comes here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and in incision; and it is in two ways, of which one is in its middle semblance, and of that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the head of the abscess is different from that of the foundation, and the appendix at the root is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, until the bow is dead according to its achievement; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are crusted, and do not die according to their achievement, as in the case of an abscess that is in a delicate joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from the joints, and leave them as they are, in case the ligature and nerve of the joint are corrupted, so this is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is from the main limb, and you delay perforation as long as it is dead, so it will harm the main limb; or if it is from the foundation, then let it be pierced in such a way that it does not come to complete digestion, lest that which is from the foundation rot completely and be poked out from within, and a fistula come; and cannot heal in great terms.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time for perforating the abscess which is dead according to complete digestion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the stabbing of the top of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it is most dependent on the abscess, and there where it opens; and let the perforation be made from the long of the neck, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all of them equally where it is not blistered.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where they bleed, according to which limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the middle, so that it is necessary to leave the piercing until it has been completed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, if you keep the body extended in its flow from it, and is full of dirty water; and by chance harden the lips and the depth of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to which limbs they need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many splits according to the appearance of their size; and if there are such abscesses where they need to be chewed, and covered up; when they have become as tough as cloth, and are softened, it is done as with blisters: and if there are any that are split into three angles, and if there are any that are covered like a apple, as with abscesses of the ankles; and if there are any that are cut in a circle, and other sizes and a covering shape.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechef; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the hopes may jump sometimes with the release of the bow, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this ointment with great care, and when you have pricked your abscess, if the wound is small, then bandage it with linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there are many pus-filled cavities, then put a patch on each one so that they touch each other; and if you have torn some of the skin around the abscess, then sew it up; and if you have stuffed some of the skin with wet hair, then pack it tightly with dry cotton or linen rag until the next day; then wash it, and treat it with ointment until it is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is an escape of blood from the cut, then bring cold water and wet the fabric, and put it on the place that is bleeding, again and again.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the escape of blood persists, then bring government and cure, and the powders that I said to put in the ears in this book, and if it is an ear, and the ear is nervous, let you know that you put on your clothes and drapes wet with wine and oil warm; and if it is in the ear, and the ear is fleshy, then let you know that you soak your drapes in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil for three days, as we have said; and then wash the abscess and dry and cure, as it should be, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally for the treatment of abscesses; or I told you how one should go before the treatment of abscesses, and see this paste.
des soros	wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the head begins to give small abscesses, and is handled by us so that it is in a mess, as much like a glove as a shoulder joint, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and those where there is moisture as well, and if they are hard and bony at the base, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose itself.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you experience with every instrument called "trimmer", from which the shape comes next, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if the wind blows from above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, if it does not leave the hair that contains this moisture, because it returns to its place when left nothing; then dip in cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; otherwise, in water and vinegar, and employ the wound, and leave it until another day; and heal those who are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the cotton has finished, on the second day, and the tar, as long as you know that it does not stay overnight; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for the case, until he is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, if the wound is in this form, let it go; and pour your oil, and peel all over, and apply all your cure to draw out the puss or where it lies; and if the artery makes you contrary, do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so do with the abscess if it is painful, and with the tailor and with the healer as I have said to you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the painful abscess and on the moist one, if it is lighter, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or chief place have no moisture, and of these two abscesses that I struck the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as a heavy stone, sharp and white, and could not break it; and if any of them had been hit, it would also have caused a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come from the head, it is necessary that those who come from the children and the roots of the ears should be completely opened, so that the bow can come out; and heal them as they should.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Several times has there been an abscess in the throat, and it has gone to the ears, and to the neck, and never comes to another place or to the chest, and is swollen, and are infected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every scrofula is properly inside its rib, as the neck and the abscess at the throat, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulae are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are those that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in those that one can see of good disposition in the neck, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and does not move from any part and is not deep; so that you must cut it from above, and scorch each part, and the two lips of the mouth are together at one end if you need it, as we have said in regard to the abscesses in the throat; and scrape little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and is not too deep either, lest the hand escape, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it will not let you sew, then put vitriolic acid on it, or some powder that stops the bleeding, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calm, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has calmed, if you return to your work, as long as you do it; then feel with your index finger whether there are any small sores, if they are, pick them and clean them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a big vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not right that you should cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double knot, and let it hang down without hurting; then wrap the wound in old linen dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover all the scar, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them up; then there should be no delay because of the abundance of the scar.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you hear to cover the root of it, and draw forth firmly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scars that have excess fluid, cut them so they die; and cut them as we have said before, depending on them, then arrange tendrily and carefully, so that it does not corrode those who are delayed from corruption; and when the wound is well washed, cure with ointment, careful to cover it.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old said and spoke about the stretching of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and that is the scriptural word of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	A those who have squint, it is fitting that the flap of the throat which is called the "epiglottis" be removed; and one shall not seek aid from this, since all the veins and the palatine bone of the sick person are to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two Mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the palatine bone, it is fitting to cover the epiglottis so that the strangulation which comes from the obstruction does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it with III circles or IV a small incision from the top, between II circles or by the quantity of the incision in the throat, not in the cartilage; and this is suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis so that there is no blade, and the vessel is long to prevent it from breaking.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, so that he extends the skin of the throat to all its length, then he splits the larynx as far as it comes to the voice box; and avoid the blood vessels from blood, if you see nothing, and then apply the medicine to it, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the fluid of the voice box that goes out by the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice. And leave the wound open for a piece.

Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuca says that we should not do this as long as the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default leaves him.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then take care of the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe, and thus is protected from death; and to order the elder to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he ordered to stitch up the wound and heal, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife and put it in her throat, and cut some of the glands in her throat; and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and I saw that she had not cut a vein but only her throat, and her veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it as long as it was well; and there came to the maiden nothing but that she grew red in the face, and returned to her normal state; so I said to myself that, in the surgery of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernia of the throat is called "gastric hernia," and it is a large hernia of a yellow color, most common in women; there are two types: congenital and acquired; there is no cause for congenital hernia.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two ways, so that one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other way is similar to an abscess which comes from us through the arteries; and there is fear, and he cannot do anything but cut it off entirely, if it is large, as we cut off fat, and examine and search all the internal organs: if you find it like this too, as I found some, and there is none at all, then cut it off, and take care well, and treat it so that it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to describe ourselves, which I will now explain in full; and it is important that we understand the clear distinction between our nature and that of an alien.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever and chills are due to the rising of the blood heat, which is complete when the perspiration is accomplished; then rest the fever and the chill.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no fever or chill or pain, and it begins to sweat, which is according to the color of the blood, and it also starts like a bud and becomes fat; and it is according to its appearances, whether thin, or wet, and its color is very different from that of the alien, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat the patient's illness, you must first test and question all the instruments called 'manipulators', according to their form or paste that is applied afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for the incision of an abscess is that you squeeze out or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers slowly and slowly, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the intruder, and take care not to go too far.

Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char. If it does not stay in place, it returns to us many times; and if it stays for a little while and does not cause you any pain, then employ some corrosive powder on the wound, extract it, and apply warm oil of chamomile, and cure it with other treatments until it heals; and if we are very ill, then cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure it from char.

des apostemes des asselles	of the tendons of the heel

Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez. de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is tight above it, then often an abscess forms, and all of it runs into the opened vein and an abscess; and if you recognize it for an artery, then the abscess is long and even; and when you feel it with your two hands, you feel a movement; and when it is for a vein, then you feel a release apparently; and it is foolish to plug this abscess, and terribly so when it is dislocated in the tendons, and at the ankles, and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is fitting that the treatment of iron be avoided, and that the one who is chief also be avoided, and in that which swells up from an artery cut from above the skin; then work on the abdomen as a snake, and carefully separate the artery from the threads, as long as it remains uncovered; then insert an awl, and let it pierce all the way to the other side of the rib cage, and take the artery with two threads; according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then press down the place where there is tension between the two ties of a thread as long as what is between them comes out; then cut off the aposteme; then bring the treatment that has been prepared in advance, as long as the tie chokes; then treat that which is coming from the ointing, as long as it is healthy; and if the aposteme is to be taken away, so that you hold what remains with your hand, then take the awl and insert it into the place where you are holding it in your hand, and let it pierce, and there are two threads; so that you pull it from the other side of the rib cage; then tie the aposteme together, as I have told you, or tie one of the two parts to the two ties of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another awl into all of the thread that is above the skin, and take the threads in four places; then cut off the aposteme until the superfluity comes out, then cut off the superfluity from the cure and leave what remains tied; then put it on a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, and bring cures for tentances and ointments as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, when they come from the artery and the vein, they come from the nerves when they are wounded, or by too much work, and similar things.

des grosses boces pendans	The big bellies hanging down
