Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second one is due to give birth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to keep her hair tied back, and then make her turn her head from side to side, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she faints because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not work, then I can try, and I will make a cup or pot with a spout from which the steam will come out into the mother's mouth, as if it were vaporized; then I will put one tube or spout in the pot, and the other in the mother's mouth, and I will let the vapors rise inside the mother; then I will make her turn her head so that she vomits what is inside her, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If one has a second wound.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If she remains after this cure and is not better, order her to soak her left hand in oil of rosemary or musk for a long time, and then let it go, and if she finds the second wound, then squeeze and stretch it little by little correctly so that the marrows do not break; but you must move it slightly from side to side, and then pull it out; if so, it will fall off.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marrow is swollen and tight, we have spoken about the cure of sneezing and inhaling herbs; and if she does not respond to all that we have said, you must be careful not to make a mistake when you pull it out; but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the marrow, you tie him to the woman's belly, then cleisterize with ointment of four-fold tallow; if so, she will sneeze and recover, but nevertheless, when she sneezes, a bad odor will come out of her stomach and head, and she will be pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is appropriate then let there be smoke-cations that are convenient for him: no one of the ancients has tried the smoke-cations of nettle and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumes the woman at the holding of the flowers and of the second one if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like to see a dog, and one puts the thin head in the nature, and the chaps wide on the fire; and let be the smoke-cations on the coals, and the tan until it is used up, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet had the foundation pierced, but it is pierced by a subtil surgery: if it is appropriate then at the ball that he pierce that surgery to his right, and does not pierce him with a spatumile acquired, and seal the wound so that he does not touch; then put on another wet one in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until he is well.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not recover, put or pierce a cane of plunk, and let him hold his hands up, and let the bone be set when he goes to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And no sudden recovery comes from a wound or abscess; if it is covered suddenly: if it is cured, as we have said of the cane of plunk.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nadation, and more painful than those that come from the base of the foundation in two parts, whether it is one or more; and when this nadation is old, if it is opened, and then moistened with a white or subtle poultice, and never does these fistulas persist; and they are caused by what is discharged or wind from the patient when he makes egestion, and by chance in salt water.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it pierces to the bladder, and only to half of the penis; and reach up to the join of the loins, and only up to the knuckle of the hand.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And then recognize that the fistula penetrates to the foundation, and not further; and it is so that you pierce your little finger or foundation, and pierce a small needle of gold or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you pierce a tent of gold or a mane of horse as far as you feel the tent or mane in your little finger; and if you do not feel it, there will be no piercing pain or wind or sight, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates only up to the bladder or up to the urinary conduit, if the urine leaps out, and cannot be controlled by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced only up to the joint of the thigh, then the effort should come only up to its place. If there is no twist and the pain does not come from within, then as soon as it has been bowie'd [bowied?], there is no medicine or immediate relief by feeling; and in these persisting fistulas there is no cure but work, and vanity of foolish men who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not persisting and are not old, there is hope of health by surgery, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his loins, and his loins are bent towards his belly; then pour a shower of rain, or of water if there is any twist, until you know where the effort comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foot, then it is appropriate that you place your index finger on it and feel for the tendon; and so that you can find out whether it has been torn or not, you will feel between your thumb and the finger, and so you know that it is persisting; if it does not work, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	If the patient feels pain in the foot, then it is appropriate that you place your index finger on it and feel for the tendon; and so that you can find out whether it has been torn or not, you will feel between your thumb and the finger, and so you know that it is persisting; if it does not work, then it cannot be healed. On the other hand, there are some that can be very well healed, but this only happens sometimes; and the help that is given to them is that, according to the width of the fistula, a fine fire should be made; and pour it directly into the fistula, as much as necessary to stop the pain at the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that those charred feathers are burned, which look like an eagle's feather; and then cure the wet blisters by wrapping them in bandages, so that those blisters turn black, then bind them with ointment, joining the blister and the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healthy, then it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is sick, then it is good; and if he tries to get between them, and does not pierce all the way up to the root which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of tar or of oil between the two, and you see the fistula at that place where the covering comes off from the root; then the handle of the entrapment of the fistula, and press it back before the covering, and then apply the cautery afterwards, as long as it comes up to the top of the covering; and then the covering will be torn away, and there will remain nothing but a small spot; then have made for yourself tar-made hats that look like an owl's feather, and there shall be none left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sun does not shine on him, and he cuts between you and the work, then the fire cautery or the medicinal potion will cut it.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c'est a savoir, l'arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l'esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when he has been restored, then he is healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes only to the foundation, and is removed from the heart, it causes him great pain; and ask those who know.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	And if you feel the tent, and between is the towel or the cloth or the sack, or it is ready to pierce, there are only two ways of hope and engagement: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it just to the foundation, or you pierce it little by little as first; and do not go too far in complete healing, so that you cover the covering which holds the foundation, and let the discharge come voluntarily; then heal it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean up after it has been cut from the foundation, or with a tent or another instrument used; then burn off that rotten wood which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and delay the fistula in the part away from the foundation: this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are no times when there are fistulas according to this way: and it is when you patch the tent in the fistula, and it is or it costs from the base of the delicate skin on top, so take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I patch I thread wrong in 2, and patch the tent all along the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin at the base inside, then remove the thread of that pierced, so that you patch your two at the base; and tie the head of the thread, and join the two shoulders together, and draw them apart, and leave it for a day or two; and do not restrain it, until the thread catches those hairs that are between the two, and chaffs; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce in all ways that you can, unless it is too much perfumed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make the lacing cover it perfectly, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is well.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the sputum with thorns from which one makes a fistula is too aggressive for one side and not aggressive enough for the other; and because it does not suit to cover completely what should be covered, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	For hemorrhoids are in two ways: either they are inside the fundament, as grain of resin, and there are little and big ones, and some are dry, and others moist but not too much, and they have a color like that of the body; and the cure for those who are inside the fundament is such that you command the patient to strain himself in order to go to the chamber, until the fundament goes away, and the thread comes out; if you hurry, and hold it with tweezers, or with your fingernail, then cut off its roots; and if it does not hold itself by its moisture, take it by a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of calico; and pull them towards your fingers, then cut them off, and powder them with some hot powders that are in the fire for cauterizing; or you cauterize them as we have said in the chapter of cauterization, since they can be cured by other treatments until they are well; and if the fundament cannot come out, so it is cleansed with a strong enema and harsh, so that it comes out freely; when the patient feels pain, and the thread comes out from the fundament, then the cure is light; and it is that you hold them with your fingernail or tweezers, cut off, then cure as we have said, until they are well, and avoid the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you prepare the wound in this way: take a tortuous thread, and bottle it into a needle, and then wind the thread over and pierce the needle from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread around the needle, and if it is wide; then pull the thread into shape, and tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave it to flow blood; then put a moistened drape on the foundation, soaked in oil or wax, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest. And then let him rest until he is hemmed, and when he has healed, cure him with ointment and other cures until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	doux
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 종종 장의 끝에서 건조함이 발생하고, 자연스럽게 변비가 생기며, 병에 걸린 사람이 나이가 많고 의약품은 도움이 되지 않습니다.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you need to cut the bark off a tree or your nail, which should not be allowed to rot; then cure it as long as it is sound so that it does not rot again; and if it cannot be cured, then start to scrape it more strongly than before, until it heals and the bark has been removed; then cure it as long as it is healthy.
dou fremit	The patient should suck on a cold compress.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	For a small piece of wood to rub against the body thoroughly, and one can feel it all over the body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the doctor should take a feather from an goose, or a strong vultur's feather, and put that feather on the friction, until the purple circle surrounds the entire area; then turn your hand over the entire feather as you chop it all around the area, and put it in place, and scrape the friction from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this of a dog's head or iron according to this form, and be subtle and run on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And do not hit it, so that you keep him in two places, and press it: And if you see, so cauterize the pain, as he is before or chapter of cauterization of fire.
de la forme dou clistere	from the form of the clistere
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time made one clistere of silver or oakwood, or melted bronze or brass; and no time made these instruments small and large, according to these which are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then, on that one bring in the cure of infants and who are feeble and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clistere small and big if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say that there is a distention where the belly is tied, so you see, and the loins are pierced from within; and one of the sides is split, and in the other; and let the belly where one lays medicines from a bladder of cow or parchment, and pierce all around the small splits, and leave between each split a space of X inches, then pour into these splits a strong string of thread twisted in X shape: and when the medicine is inside, if it adheres to the instrument before a strong string, then draw out; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil or amberwax or some other thing with which to grease the head of the cystere, then pour it lightly; then the ministers stretch their two hands together so that he is all full, then remove the head of the cystere, and raise the legs of the patient against the wall, and let the medicine come out as much as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you bandage it in a disease of decay from the abdomen, and the medicine hastens to come out, if you continue it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the root or abscess, so is the cautery also fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine cautery where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made, and according to their places where they are made, and because of this.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things because of which wounds are made are by hitting with a stone, and cutting with a sword or a knife, or a lance or a club or a stake, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that splits on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes where the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or a similar thing, and the skin is torn all around, and the wound is large, and you doubt about the abscess being hot: if you do this quickly, he will heal from the head itself if the blood comes only from the wound, and the healing will be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and deny the patient wine and fatty meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not heal, if his meat is reduced, and he does not drink wine, nor eat cheese; and put on the wound, if an abscess forms, wet it with oil and vinegar, or with stinging wine; and if there is no abscess, if the wound is fresh and not moved by the wind, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he has moved it, put on some onions, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as a sword-blade and similar, the lips cannot be sewn together smoothly, but must be sewn together roughly, as I will say to the wounds of the belly from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and can only be held together with a few stitches, then sew the wound with medicine and restore it with hard cloth instead of leather; and order the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles and roasted wheat, as well as poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find leather rotting, and it has reached the bone, then sew it tightly, and pour it strongly, then heal it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and that you put this powder which hardens as the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and the powder finely, and apply the wound, and bind it together, as long as she is well healed and joins all her blood; and then bind it tightly, and leave it undissolved, if it swells; for we do not tie the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no one makes this powder only, unless one has incense and dragon's blood, but the fire moves it.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, surely it is clean, unless one puts some of this powder on it; but put on some digestive oil or flour of barley made with water and honey until it is dry; then treat it with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the throat, and there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the throat is cut where the artery lies:
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the throat that is affected, then there should be no other intention but to allow the wound to heal, and not to place anything restraining upon it, for this would hinder healing and cause withdrawal; and nothing should be placed on the wound except what is cold, for the substance of the throat is cold, and its connection with the skull, which is the highest limb, is through the jaw; but let the medicine be as warm as mutton washed in soft water, and mixed with oil of roses, and let it be washed also in soft water, and other small stones according to this manner, and let it be anointed with moist oil.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bandage it tightly and treat until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full ofbowels, then pierce or cut deeper; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows, so that it dries up and turns black, and cauterize that way; and if the inflammation in the throat is cut, or damaged, and the direction is guarded, so that the meat goes, if the juice is cut high on the jaw of the throat, and does not touch the throat but sets it back to its natural shape; and then tie tightly, and leave it for a few days, then treat with ointments which are useless until it is healed; and if the wound has impressed into the bone, then pierce it; and if there are pieces of bone, then push them up hard, and those that you cannot push, then leave them until the wound festers and comes out in its own way; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle with powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound, and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in the previous chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look out for wind-purging in the patient: because then the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep and is fresh to all its vital power, then do not put on powder at first, nor bind it so that it does not move perfectly, and return to the core, and ease the pain; but put on an ointment, and bind it II times a day; and if you have no ointment, put in the wound dry cotton to soak up the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for III days, or IIII, or more often; then you will not get spasms or bad tremors from the core; and when you see the bones in good positions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the cancer with drugs and other treatments as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot be cured, operate, then tie up that which has become a fistula; do so as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a spear or knife and it is deep, stitch it up; if it is shallow, use powder, and if it has broken into pieces of bone, mend the wound, and the sharp ends, if they are sticking out; and if they are not sticking out, let them fester, so that there will be less extraction work; and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Abdominal rupture is great and large and small; from a big wound, the intestines sometimes come out, or the intestines are caught by the cut, so the entry of air is stopped, and the stitch is less difficult, and no more than a small wound hurts them; because if we do not put them back together, step by step, they swell up so much that they feel cold, then we put them back together, and for smaller wounds, it is the same as for bigger ones, so I will say each one separately and will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines has come out, there are two ways to deal with it: either because the wound is small, as we have said; or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in one of the following ways: dip a sponge or a thin cloth in warm water only; or cook it in warm wine and cumin and spice, and remove the intestine as much as it swells; and never stop doing this, and let it rest that it may cool down.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling disappear, if you moisten the intestine with water or with wine and herbs are cooked, because by this it is softened a little; and if it cannot enter, then cut a little hole in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to let it rest, that we do not cut it unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for it: if you cut it from within and take it away, and look at it like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are protruding, if you can reset it according to its natural shape in its proper place, for this is difficult to do.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the part near the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part near the navel, then put the head and chest higher than the parts near; and so one should treat what I have said in large and painful wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you should prepare the patient, then take two hands and insert a needle filled with thread into the wound from its back part; gather the lips together; and this is the common way of sewing, and it is necessary that you press one side of the wound, and take a strong thread; then pierce the skin on both sides of the wound with a needle, keeping the space between them consistent; then make an X-shaped stitch to join the two edges; finally, take another double thread, pass it through the needle from two directions, leaving a little gap between each stitch; continue this way until you have covered all the wound; and the needles should be medium size, because small ones can easily go through the skin, while large ones cannot enter well; for this reason, it is necessary to use medium-sized needles; do not insert the needles too far into the flesh or skin, so that they do not pierce and cause the wound to open before it is sewn together; then secure the needle ends, so that they do not sting the patient while he sleeps; and place a cloth or bandage over the needle ends to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound has healed; and this way of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds; because, if you sew one side of a large wound, you will need two needles and a strong thread; and when you have pierced both edges of the wound with the needle, join them together with an X-shaped stitch; then take another double thread and pass it through the needle from both sides, leaving a little space between each stitch; continue in this way until all the wound is sewn together; and these needles should be medium-sized, because small ones can easily go through the skin, while large ones cannot enter well: for this reason, medium-sized needles are necessary; and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh or skin, so that they do not pierce and open the wound before it has been sewn together; then secure the needle ends, so that they do not sting the patient while he sleeps; and place a cloth or bandage over the needle ends to hold them in place; and leave them until the wound has healed.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine when it had been outside for 22 hours, and the wound was縫ed together after 15 days, and I healed it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle was that he did not die, and I did not heal it with ointment, because I was in a place where there was no ointment to be found, nor any medicines; and I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water as long as he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two ways of stitching: take the needle and pierce it from the outside in to the middle; when it has gone through the flesh, turn the thread so that it comes out on the other side of the wound; and the understanding of this stitch is such that you sew just as the skin-layerer does with fur, and leave one end of the thread on one side, and take up the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which Galen dealt with properly, if it is so that there is no font, which joins the two parts together in a natural way, and applies one of the heads to the other head in such a way: thread a needle from the tip of one of the heads nearest the mirach, and pierce that hole only, leaving the two heads joined; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside part jusc’à celui dedens, through the two heads; then pierce each of them from the outside part jusc’à celui dedens, in the two other heads that are on the other side; and this is the manner of sewing with the blade and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And for this Galen has such a word, and no one testifies against it: that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, or there should be thread in each; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew leather; and know that when the rupture is at the belly's end, such a stitch is more painful than any other.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l'ait muee, si remet arer l'intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l'ait muée, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu'il soit sané; et se tu n'as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu'elle comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant qu'il soit sané.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in most cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten another light thing in tempred oil or rose oil, and place it around the joints, and burn the pads; and if pain or pus appears in the balls, and often happens, then wash them with black wine, and most surely the pus comes up to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "jejunum", cannot heal when they are torn, and this is because of the location of veins, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and because it approaches its nature to that of a newborn.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the flesh jumps out of the wound, put it back behind just as the intestine is, while it is fresh; and if it has become old and has turned black, you must find the place that is black, from which no blood comes, because there are veins and arteries; then cut between the two bones, and hang them from the side of the wound until the extraction jumps out, and the wound bleeds.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, you can restore it in some cases, as if someone were torn by an arrow or a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became convoluted and turned into a fistula, and there was vomiting and wind; I put on it according to what I could, and did not cease to apply subtility until it healed, and sewed up the incisions.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him mend, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly; and there was no evil, but tarried in better dispositions, and feasted and drank; and said no experimenters that when he has a little wound in the intestine, it should be bound somewhat: take sharp things from great testes, then bring the lips of the wound together, and when the sharp things have opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that she draws her mouth out; and then he takes hold of the head, and this remains so that he cannot release it, then puts another sharp thing after in the same way as before, until the wound is all taken care of; and let the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is burnt in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal in some way: take the chief of this thread of intestine that has been almost severed, and then bind to the chief of this thread a fine tortuous linen thread, then bring the thread out in the needle, and in cutting the intestine, and bring it back at the rupture; and this method of stitching with sharp things is not as strong as along the course of the fetus and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, most certainly when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no cure or medicine unless subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	I know that any wound or abscess, as soon as it heals, is called universally a "fistula", and more so when it has been lanced and drained.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to the true definition a hard and white nodule, where there is no pain, and it is also lanced like the feather of an owl; and never completely clear bowels, and sometimes thick, sometimes thin; neither has it ever been seen, and on the other hand enough; and I have not spoken of the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no relief, this is only because of one of the VIII causes: namely, smallness of blood or cors; or for its wickedness; or because it has too much bowels inside, and on the lips, which does not allow the birth of bowels; or because there is too much bowels; or because the lees are rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good in the cure; or because, that which is caused by a pestilence, or because the propriety in the region is late digestion, and slow sanctity, and escapes by nature; or because there are veins or osses: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make known to you the cure for fistula, which is done by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula may occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sinew, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes that it affects the principle limb, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of great difficulty in the cure, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the surface that I have mentioned, and you have promised to cure it, and you see it clearly, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, look at it; and if the fistula is twisted, look at it with a slender tent of lead, for the lead bends in accordance with its curvature; and if the fistula has broken hands, and you cannot cure it well with tents, then cauterize it according to what I have said, and oste the broken bones and corrupt tendrils that are inside; and then cure it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right place, then it is necessary that you cure it completely, as well as you can, then put wet tents in medicine water, and pour them out to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that is reserved at the bottom; and then put oilmens in wringing fresh oil, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cauterize it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If in the shoulder there is a hurt to the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackening, so long as the decay is all through the bone, then heal it with healing stuffs until it is whole; and if it is not whole, and it continuesbowed, as before, know that you have not gone far enough: if you discover and seek out until you are at the bottom, and take away all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is whole there, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too great that you cannot come to it; if there is no other problem than to let it heal naturally; and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out by the claws, if you extract it with the right tool for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them out, one by one; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut and moisture and heal it, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you do not remove them in an hour, then place something on the wound that will cause putrefaction, and let it be until the hairs rot around the bone, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then wait so long for corruption until the blackness covers all the bone, then dress the wound; and if there is a great deal of corrosion and it comes up to the root of the bone; then make sure it is covered completely until the corrosion is gone, and then treat it until it is healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that entered the bone, so that the matter came to the leg, and was escaped by a large abscess, and had no apparent reason for opening it; but because of his folly, it opened so much that much matter came out, and became a fistula, and it came to such a point that all went away wet with water from the bone; and many times he was cured in two years, and there was no cure for it in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines that were used to cure it, and that which flowed through the openings had made the bone very red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and I found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and put into one of the holes as much as I could discover a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perciet, and it came against corruption all the way inside; I knew what appeared to me of the bone, and I took care that there was no other corruption, besides that which I had; and I began to restore the wound with medicines in a long time, and I could not bind it; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I knew it, and then I took it out, and I leaned over the hole; but I did not put as much into it as I could reach with a palm of the bone, and I set it back with medicines; and it was healed and bound firmly, and it came not again to open the wound for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death which I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir. Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	For the cutting, it is according to this way: arise first the leg of the warm water very well, until the big blood is thin, then extract the leg of the sick from above the crotch up to the knee; then open the vein at its base, or in two or three places, with a wide cut, then draw out and draw out the black blood by your hand, from one head to another, as much as the virtue of the sick can bear; and then tie it up, and command that he be covered with meat, wearing black collyers; and restart the evacuation and treatment when the veins are clean, and wash the sick.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
