Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it is seen twisted and twisted and wrapped together, and is not straight, as we have said, it is necessary that you split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And if the shape of the iron with which you cover the vis is twisted, and does not split it, but covers the vein; and is of a thick form, for if it were thin, you would split the vein, but if it is thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this causes the skin to rot, as if it were crawling under the skin and between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the onset of this disease are that an extremely large inflammation comes in the leg, then the joints change, and the vein begins to break forth, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And if the veins open, then you should wrap a piece of cloth around one and a half hands' length from the head [of the leg], and tie it, and leave the cloth wrapped around for as long as it takes for the swelling to go down; then untie it and cut it off, leaving nothing behind. For if you cover it over completely, it will turn into an abscess and putrefaction, and cause great disease; so it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the knuckle, and there is no remaining [swelling] after treatment. And this disease has happened to me five or six times when the veins were opened up to five hands' lengths, and when I cut them, they burst out [or broke open], and all the contents came out; and it was emptied, and medicine for putrefaction was applied every day, then that wound was treated just as the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at no time to this vein hands rain, and least of all when it opens in the ankle of the foot, or where the foot is, and then it comes out of the breach, and from which it rains; so treat it if you will as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between leather and shield
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buff disease", for it often occurs in buffaloes, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and shield, and goes everywhere ascending and descending, and feels good at the sensation of one member to another, until it rips the skin where it went, and comes out; and is infected with pus, as if it were worms and scorpions and insects and scabies; and doubt is caused by its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the oil, by chance it enters and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it and draw it out, only then can you do so: if therefore you lay the joint above and fasten it firmly, then lift it up and draw it out, and let it fall into the vessel in which you are working, and you will not find it unless you cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it spoils the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming to the head near the oil, then squeeze it out tightly, and then lift it up and draw it out. And it is necessary to use the patient's own corruption of medicines to dissolve the bad humors and sear with meat腐烂.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and moves from member to member; and I have seen the one that I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman, and I uncovered her arms, and saw a little swelling in the vein of her arm; and then suddenly, I felt it go up as high as a worm to her shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if it were alive and silver when it moved from its place; the pain left that place, and entered into her shoulder, and then a little while after, it corroded all over her body until it came to her other arm; then she told me that she was turning herself round in her bed, just as I had seen her do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how she moved from member to member, for I have never heard of this disease in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have often heard of people with this disease having pain move from one part to another, but I did not expect it to happen in this way, as it did in the woman; and I thought that perhaps her body was so constricted that the wind went up and down inside her, and because her veins were uncovered and her body damp.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see that this disease is cured and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we said, above and with care, and then cope up to so that those winds stop at their place; and cauterize that place; and if you do not see that wind in your hair, if you cure it with dirty pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	They are various, according to their appearances and according to the places where they come from.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is such that there are some with large points, and small, and curly, and soldered; and those that have two angles, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces; and some that do not chore in any member at all, but chore according to two ways: first, in the principal members, as brain, liver, pancreas, stomach, kidneys, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she dies in any of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, get to know: if it is necessary that you wash yourself from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after many preparations; and when this bad sign does not get to know you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the sign of the skull is that the arrow pierces the bone, and the medicine that lies on the skull, is when the scotomatous and sad and twisted and red eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of food; and perhaps it does not come from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and when the wound appears moist and white like blood, and looks like burnt charcoal; and if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the sitter when she lies down is that she is near the left breast, and also because it feels like she is lying on something hard, not empty; and perhaps the sitter moves as much as a bird does, in short black breath, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: so that one can doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that has pierced the heart is that there is no foam of blood that jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he sighs heavily and feels cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the back, it is a delight to the little ribs; and there is great pain and sorrow and sighing; and all the members shake.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps there is nothing coming out of the wound from the digestion.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the belly, and there is no end of it in the gut, then there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and the urine flows out and runs away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is affected like this, the face, neck, throat, shoulder, jaw, back, and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it does not move, tell me if you have done something different.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me that an arrow entered someone's neck at the root of their neck: I tried to extract it, and I pushed it from another side away from the fat of the ear, and was healed with no pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tie a string around the arrow that lies in the fat of oil paper, and the string was tied up, and I could not achieve more than the tip towards the stalk, and the string was big like an arc-turquoise, all very light without ears; The game was healthy, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I tied a string from the throat to a Christian, and the string was Arabic to ears; I knew the beards, and I waited until I tied it up, and the Christians were healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I tied a string to a man at home, which was a head or stomach, and I thought he was dying; and then after thirty days, if his condition did not improve, I cut the string, took it out, and tied it up again, and it did not cause any bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to see a man who has an arrow in his body or foot, and the wound is deeply set; then let the arrow stay inside, and do not disturb its natural course, nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was deeply set; and thus he suffered great pain; and many more such things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I healed a king's son who had an arrow in his neck, and the arrow was deeply lodged; it hung slightly to one side; and the arrow was all bloodied. I was called to heal after that which had been shot three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	And I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I left it there for a whole night, and I felt nothing; but he felt stinging and pain on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was the point of the arrow I put on top of the plaster with the atractive and digestive, so that the leeches do not inflame; and I saw the leeches of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster at once, and resolved the wound immediately, and delayed it for a long time so that he felt the arrow inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the corrosive water medicine at once, until it was opened, and tried it out, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened to its place; then I inserted it into the opening of the wound with that medicine until the shape of the head of the arrow came out clearly; and three months later, then the wound spread so much that I had to pull out the pliers from one side and another, and could not remove it; so then I kept on trying and devising ways of instruments, until I got one with a nice form, so that I removed it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage from the nose cannot be healed; so I healed it, and the wound was sewed up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Have you explained the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your cure on this which I have not said, because the liber is unable to do everything; but the master surgeons compare on a very small thing, and on those who are present and fail, try nine or ten operation, and nine or ten instrument, for the dissection of foreign things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are in the members or they are stuck unless according to two ways: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which jumps out is a running arrow in their bones, and never is at any time stuck now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not bend now, let it remain so that the bones are rotten inside, and the outlet is open; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, so leave it for a certain number of days, and every day it bends; and then it bends, and if it does not bend, so pierce all the small veins around until the blood comes out, and then cut.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the neck bone and goes to one of the head's vertebrae, and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it so that it remains even after a few days, because if the arrow comes out to the skin, death is certain.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and not out to the skin, and stays there for a few days without any bad accidents, then use the pulling device.

Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement. Healthcare that prevents diseases does not have a specific time determined, but rather should be done at any hour or moment; and it is not necessary to take care of children before they are twelve years old and women except for the fourth month up to seven months.

Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	They must not save the old people who have passed sixty years. When someone is to be saved, in whatever way it is possible that he should not break the intestines of a light clister, if he has held back the wind, so that the intestines do not attract the superfluous pus that injures the main members; nor must he be saved if he is too soured by meat, or if he is yvring (pregnant), as much as it is possible, nor if he is drooping, and if he has had a passion of colic, vomiting, and cramping of the belly, and frequent lying with a woman, and travail, and staying up late, and this and that, or by something in the arms or heart; then subtilely the humors, let him be fat, by meat, drink, and medicine, if he can benefit from it; then go into or bathe, if nothing helps to soothe his pain, and save him from the vein at the pit of the stomach, as we have said; and keep him away from work, and hunger, and lust, and similar things; and be careful and join, and let him who is to be saved be higher than those whom one saves, and rub his arms twice or three times, then draw the tendon above moderately, because when it is too stiff or weak, he cannot bend it; and then rub the savior with his right hand at the vein where he is to be saved, a little or a lot, that the vein does not burst and bleed; then moisten the savior with flame from a small bit of old oil, and put his thumb of his left hand on the vein where he is to be saved, so that the vein may not burst and bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventosité, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if it opens the vein for the first time, it is good; and if not, then it begins again a little bit more of that way or another in which the veins are inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed and the patient hopes for it, let him rest a day or two, and do not bind his arm: perhaps he will get pus; don't enter or bathe, then begin again the treatment if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the cut subtilely, and you doubt that it won't come out as much pain as you see, so firmly in that wound itself to the whole flame properly; and work a little hospital, so that the veins are inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros. Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant. Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting on any of what we have said, for perhaps in the heart without the artery; but make it dry with plaster to harden the place, then heal with other healing, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each pain according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the pain is black, let it run until it is red; and if you see too much, let it run until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who has a sore and is out of the way, and needs bloodletting, that he make a larger wound and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and heal him little by little, and let him heal across, not through piercing; and this mode of healing is saved from bloodletting and nerve injury, and it is better than long healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant. Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he sweats in the sickness, after the flow of blood, it is necessary that he smell brew from char, and fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up blood sometimes, and feels faint at other times, when he is weakened by great sickness, that he be healed little by little, according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.

Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who faints elsewhere, if he must heal him two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement. Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it alone and do not squeeze it, as long as the abscess is calm.
