Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that goes into the arm is cut at the base of the arm because it is composed of many veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of this incision is that the patient holds his hand in hot water until the color turns red; then let it cool down a little, so that the vein appears well, and then incise across it, not wide nor long; and if it is too large, incision near the joint of the hand, and do not take it out, but put the hand again in hot water, and leave the blood to run in the water, as long as you have enough; and if it is in esteit, do not reboudre the hand again in hot water, for we put it more in peril than in esteit; and the incision of this vein is more saved from all other veins, than there is no artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment for the right hand's salutation is for all liver ailments, and this is how it is done: draw out the hand, and dip it in warm water until the vein disappears, if one can see it; then cut it across, and chop it completely, so that nothing hurts anything; and do not chop too much finely, lest the nerves be completely exposed, and then put the hand back into the warm water, unless it has become frozen in the wound, and cannot be taken out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have finished treating the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and silk over it to join it firmly together, and do this for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment for the left hand is good for mouse disease, and do all the same as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The disease of the sore is good for all diseases that are in the body; such as diseases of the mares, and retentive flowers, and diseases of the reins, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of this medicine is that the patient should pour some hot water on it, and rub the vein as long as it hurts, and lie down on top of the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and goes up the foot with much rain; heal the wound or more large rain, or at the ankle, that it may be cured.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, you must guard against the cold which is in the ground, and heal it in the same way as when you are walking; and let the fire go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he can't get out of it, put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the surgery needs to be done for the first time, then begin again on top of it a little bit later, because the blood is salty; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the same incision on the other leg evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and the surgery to relieve the pain in the hip is when it is for sciatica.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this surgery is that the patient goes in or out of the water, and draws it out from under the ankle with four twists, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then do all the cuts in all ways that you can, and cross them; and make sure to chop it off, for its blood is up, and it has been very well refilled by many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't open it, so that the blood does not flow out of the foot and towards the small toe, and keep away from the nerves; and make the wound bleed a little, and then pull the leg off, and put cotton on it and tie it up; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	The suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of horn, or of glass; and suction is done according to two manners: either by piercing and drawing blood, or not piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	The suction that is without piercing is made in XIIII ways of the body: one at the top of the head; and another around the neck; and another II sides of the neck; and another under the chin; and another on the shoulders; and another on the arms; and another on the legs; and another on the feet; and this suction does not deal with blood except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it is not useful, unless it be made at all times or without heat in any disease that comes from overindulgence, as long as the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it happens, or because of customs, we should ventilate each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and milm and in each decade; for there are such ones who, when they need to ventilate, have a heavy head; and those who truevent repletion and rudeness on their face, and on their head, and at the throat, and darkness in their eyes; and such ones who truevent a drop of blood from their mouth, and have escaped the tongue, and thirst for blood; and if there are such ones who think and see through not having eaten blood and Navert and Death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and more so when it is the middle of the month, we order them to ventilate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon of the head if it helps with the headache of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and does not come except after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in the place of the surgery of the head, and does not come except for those of a cold complexion who are used to it or who have a fever, because this does them great harm; and for that one does not come except at night when sleeping, nor who has a cold head disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become confused, and for this reason a suction cup should be placed a little further down due to the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the suction should be applied to the neck at the level of the recovery of the head and of the basin, and for this reason it should be placed a little higher than the place where the recovery occurs, that is to say at the level of the throat and of the windpipe, and also at the level of the stomach, and a little below; and it should be pushed in slowly, because if it is pushed too hard, confusion or indigestion may occur.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And the suction should be applied to the costlets of the neck if it causes pain in the head, and blurring of vision and dizziness, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and at the level of the recovery of the basin; and you must instruct the patient that he press his hand firmly but not too much so as not to cut off the blood from the artery, and not to cause any pain.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The winds of the mouth cause disease in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is at the level of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the shoulders cause as much pain as three veins in the arms, since they drain blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient that he not too tightly bound, for his skin is thin for the saddle, and it hurts to press and the arteries are visible.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wind that is on the back is worth as many emissions from the fundament, and similar diseases, and it is necessary that the wind be large, and of air, for it has the task of well milking; and perhaps, if it were too subtle, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventuses of the legs if they are opened wide, for they draw blood from all the body, and equal the old pains of the back, and of the knees, and of the bladder, and remove flowers; and are in place of the two sophes, and of the two ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use, and bring death in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the suction cups is that you should first put them on, and suck quickly, and then place them securely, and move them evenly, and do not stop doing this as long as you see the red and inflamed spot, and feel the pain of blood; then tighten, and remove the cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have a very tight chest, and clear pores: it is then necessary to make a large wound, and once cut, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is outside the body is large, so that consider to wound twice: the first time for subtlety open the way blood thick.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very heavy outside, so that consider to wound the third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, if we persist only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to extract blood, let us begin often; and if the outside is heavy, so that finish firmly, and the end is that the wound be perceived suddenly, and consider a man who has thick and hard skin, and who suffers it, that you oil the leas of the suction cups with oil to open and dissolve: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or soft almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lilac, or chamomile, or other.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is too much fluid, thick and cold, take oil of almonds, or of balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person has a fever and is sweating, there is no need to put oil on, but it needs to be washed after the perspiration of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or something else.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if someone has too much moisture, if he rises up with it, or with water of myrtle, and of sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And if someone has a lot of thick fluid, they should rise up with old wine, or water of oak, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not good to bathe before the wind or after bathing, but an hour or two after; and one should not sleep after perspiration, but when he needs to, when he has been perspiring.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard against those who are coleric, and their heat is too acute and inflamed; let him drink cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in the shade, and similar foods; and eat small amounts of meat, and roast pork, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and small amounts of water, and small amounts of meat, and roast poultry and fowl; and on the day when he breathes wind, he must drink more than eat; and sometimes give certain men triple or musk before or after wind to strengthen the main members; and make the heat subtle, but it only helps those who are warm.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that do not hurt are those placed on the liver, and on the side, and podagra, and on the belly and kidneys and ribs and hip; because this member does not suffer to be hurt on the joints, and it is done only so as to attract blood from one member to another, just as we put cups on the breasts when we do not feel well; in order to remove the viscous substance that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and kidneys to reduce the member; and so it removes pain, if there is an operation or a stone, it removes it by its attractive virtue, perhaps the operation or the stone has been moved from its place; and they are never filled together, and never filled with plain water, as in the disease of pleurisy, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water, or water in which herbs have been cooked suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus: It should be two hands wide and half a palm in diameter, and it should have a small hole in the center as if for a pin, as for wrapping an needle, and let it be of brass, so that it does not cut the patient when applied to the member; and in the middle it should have a cross bar of brass or iron, for holding a grip, and they should be great or small according to the disease and the age of those who take them; because the suction cups of children are other than those of old people, and of thin ones are other than those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should put this suction cup on the member: take the grip of wax or linen, and place it in front of the suction cup across the cross bar, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and these two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when one presses, the vapor comes out, and take off the suction cup; and take the grip again as before, and renew it often, if you need to do so.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the chest tubings that are used in pleurisy, there is no tube or hole, and it is only used when there is water, placed on the limb with great caution; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The chest tubings that are used in pleurisy have no tube or hole, and they are only used when there is water; put them on the limb with great care; and this is the form: Do not use them in members where you cannot place tubings because of their smallness, like lips and gums, and similar things; and in the bare skin of horses, if there are two or no hair, and others that look like them; and the quality of using them is that when you find tubings that are in sweet water without danger, take them; put them into water that is sweet, as long as they are comfortable, and have nothing in their bladders; and then clean the wound with a swab and put the tubing on; and when they become clear, and dry up, if it is possible to place a tube there, do so, for this is better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the level of this, and then of water very well, and then squeeze it; and if the levels are too far from the center of the veins, wet a linen drape in cold water, and put it on, until the veins are stopped; and if there are many veins, put crushed vitriolic stones or gall, and similar things, until they are stopped; or you can put half peeled peas on the level, and leave them to burn at the level, and now they will stop; and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the veins do not want to take it, rub the level with fresh blood, or insert an needle into it so that the vein comes out, and then put it on, and sometimes when they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they are bleeding, powder a little aloe and seared hay, or ash, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the translation of the provided text:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters on this topic are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are beneficial for dislocations and joint pains.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, oh learned one, that the wise men have never poured this substance onto themselves from ancient books or letters; and because of this, knowledge of it has been lost in our land, for I have never found any good book on it; and I know nothing about it except what can be learned from the study of ancient books, or from experience, or through custom in my life. I have described here, in this chapter, what is contained within this substance, and I have summarized it at the end; and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where the sage places his understanding, and delays on the truth, so that those who are tested can learn and understand this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when rupture or dislocation or twists or dislocates comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing else hinders you, as weakness of the corset, or entangling, or old people; or if his shoes are not very good, or too often; and have mild cold drinks, that is to say, cold jousts, and horseflesh and cheveline, and do not drink wine, or have any greasy drinks, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt about a hot apothema, or an expansion of matter in the member; if the sick person returns to his first governance that he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken nose begins to heal, it is fitting that the sick person be nourished with meat that makes good healing, or he has viscousness, as well as baked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and pie, and cow's milk, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For if one delays too long, then one will soon have a fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot well heal or hardens together by nature because of the seclusion of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, as children's bones; but there is remedy in this: when a bone is broken on one side with large pieces of flesh, which are joined to the limb, we must put them back together again so that they mend firmly; and no more of their work, and because it is necessary for such ones to have thick meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are many and various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break at the top of the head is other than the break at the foot of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes with the sawing, and another when it is sharpened, as the blade of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if a break is with a wound, and a break makes a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each way has its tool, and its own instrument in the repair, as soon as the memory comes back to its place; and is known the break of the bone by that it is twisted, and open well from one side, and presses on the hand; and when there is no twisting or bend in the neck, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture, but he may well have a twist, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not move it with the hand, but put medicines on it that come later, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in the armpit, and are the two parts separated, it is now necessary to put them in point of equality, so as the chest and i come viegne; and if the chest is hard, let him leave no day, as long as the chest is calmed down; then he puts equal to the mues that you can lightly and safely, and know that the recovery of him is more easy than the recovery of him who has pieces; then he forces it, as it should be.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are pieces, and the extension of the two parts is hand or foot, or at your hand is a small member, or II strings, or a string and at your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are set aside, you remove by all means the additions in their places at the mues that you can, and keep that by your work no lesion or pain comes to the patient; and well join the two bones of the osses according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel the pulse well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if the pulse is nice, and do not pull it too much, press so as those who make come from their overwork abscess hot and contracted member, as we have tried many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, instruct the patient that he not move it, watching or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and guard well that the member be so secure that it feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, it is not in place, and the need to put it in such a way that there is no pain; and guard well that it be put correctly, so that there is no tortuosity when he is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Car il y a petits membres, si comme bras et doigt et semblant: si convenait envelopper drapeaux de lin mou et subtile; et ceux qui sont gros, si comme cuisse et jambe: si convenait envelopper d'un liien large et dur, car les liiens larges embrassent tout le grand membre, et l'entraignent de toutes parts uniformément, si qu'il n'y a nul trou; puis le tiens entoure légèrement, III tours ou IIII selon le membre, et étire ta main un peu à tout le liien, puis va au dessus de la rupture et l'entraigne moins, que la rupture puis éloigne un peu la rupture; et adoucis le liien un peu et un peu, tant que tu appuis fort partie du lieu sain, puis reprends autre liien, et retourne entoure très-fort sur le lieu brisé; puis reviens à la partie désordonnée de la rupture, et l'entraigne modérément, ne ni trop fort ni trop mollement, si comme nous avons dit en la première lieure au dessus; puis met entre les liens enveloppés de lin ou de drapeaux, tant qu'il soit tout égal, puis le tout par-dessus le bandage, et puis met tes étapes bien faites, s'il n'y a pas d'abdication ou d'enflure.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or an swelling, if you place something soothing on the abscess, and let it sit for a few days; then draw up on your thumbs, and be half of a thumb's breadth away from the abscess, either with a piece of leather used to make cleats, or with palmyra stalks, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And if there is a fracture or a break, if you place something soothing on the fracture, and let it sit for a few days; then draw up on your thumbs, and be half of a thumb' breadth away from the fracture, either with a piece of leather used to make cleats, or with palmyra stalks, and be according to this figure: But it is necessary that the thumb that you put on the break be a little thicker and wider than the others; and be also as far away as necessary from the limb's smallness or greatness; then draw up on the thumbs just as you did at first time, and tie with a thread going forward, as in the first time on the break; tighter is better, but not too tight, and the thread should be of linen; because if the thread is thick, like the cords they make for ligatures which are twisted linen, that is a great mistake, because the fracture cannot be equal if it is too tight, and it only needs to have between each thumb half an inch of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the chaps of the stars after extraction in his healthy places, then put those scales of linen or another rag so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the rupture and the cure is broken, I will tell the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not seem right to extract stars from all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it does not seem right to put stars on them before five or seven days, or more according to the necessity of the abscess; and follow here the method of the ancient plasters for restoring rupture, dislocation, and torsion: and that is that you take flour that stays on the walls of the mill, and confound it with a lot of egg, and put this conflation, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and that is the common way of the plasterer restoring the rupture to many conditions, and most often to women and small children, for it is not too sharp nor too hard.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plastering for healing breaks, dislocations and twists: take myrrh and aloes, Z Z.; asphaltum and mastic, X X.; aconite, VIIII Z.; and make them into a powder, and blend them with sheep's wool; the mixture of the flesh is warm, so use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly heals broken bones, and is good for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plastering for healing twists: take myrrh and aloes, Z Z.; masticum and asphaltum, X X.; aconite, VIIII Z.; well grind, and confect with sharp or sheep' s wool; and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plastering for dislocated joints and broken bones to soothe the pain immediately, and use the bone size, and break up: take a new one, and soften it with water and cooked oil, and put on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	It is not good for the emollients to return, but it is good to properly soothe the abscess, and properly ease the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an ointment that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-owl leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing bone breaks and soothing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of vetches, each of them one part; and grind, and confound with wine, and the member is warmed up, and the confound with water of coriander or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that works better than the first when the abscess is persistent and comes back after healing the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and of flax, of mulleins, and of marjoram, and of violets, and of chamomile, each one or part thereof; and grind them up, and make into a paste with salt water, or with sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ipecras states that we should not put anything on a broken member to restore it but only wax and oil made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that we should put on a broken member things dry, a little warm, such as mirr, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plasters that are good for lesions and pain: take wool and feathers of the same size, or hair of a goat, and of wormwood, and of grass, and of mulleins, and grind them up, and make into a plaster, and put it on the member.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take care not to let the patient feel any pain, nor have his bone move out of place; but if pain comes to its place, or itching, or no rest or swelling, hurry and set it free, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge moist with seawater, and dip into the water, and raise up his part, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry, wet with water or oil and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and let the inflammation of the member be healed, and the pain be gone, then begin again to apply the poultice, and a little of the plaster, and do not twist it so hard as before; and keep it subtile until it is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need to apply poultices and bind it up, if it begins again, as you did for the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all of what we have said, and it is not released until after three days or four or five or seven; and never leaves it for XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the break-up approaches the shoulder socket; then hold back more than before, and let the meat fatten, if I have said before; and if you see that it is drying out more than it is necessary to do so, arise then with hot water every time you release it, and let it be for each third day, and let it drip a little of the hour; by this work then cut off the rest at the limb, and carefully fix what has been broken: it is bad, and if it is painful and fearful ovraiges, and I do not see anything else but to slow down and do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways to break the bone
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways to break a bone, and there are various shapes of fractures, and the causes are distinct; for there is a fracture that is done by the impact of an arrow or spear, which breaks all the bone up to where it becomes one with the flesh, as when it happens in the heel or foot; and this is what is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or an arrow can break the bone from above by piercing it, and this is called "absolute" fracture; and there is a wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is by impact from within, or by splitting or breaking the bone from the collarbone of stone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a perforating fracture that approaches up to the skin which is attached to the bone, or that lies on the bone, and this is the wound, great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that is located in the bone is as thin as a lock of hair, and the cut is small, so this break is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by a stone, or by a fall, or by a similar thing, and it causes a piece of bone to enter; and if the head of the lock is located as a blacksmith does when he works on a lock.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is much moisture at the base of the lock where the bone is located, so it is like the head of a child; and all these kinds of breaks are pieces of small size as they are made in locks; and I will speak about this place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of breaks by the traction on them, and the inquiry at tents, and by the corrupt cart which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by the fact that when one exposes the bone, and rubs it over, thus opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for the fracture, be careful of possible accidents, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, palmsiness, feverish ague, and the hairs stand on end, and others similar appearances in many conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a promising accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the rupture comes first to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone within the fourteen days since it happened.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must remove the bone within the seven days since it happened, so that the tissue decay not, and the accident mentioned above comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break in the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, you should split the broken part here: and it is that you press the head of the sick person, and cover it over the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more easily than you can, and if the break in the blood comes to uncover the bone, or abscesses, help him with whatever is necessary, and it is that you fill the place of the membrane wet with oil of roses; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of the breaking of the blood; then begin to split the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you split the narrow end in front, and this is its form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I bottle another length, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have many different-sized nails, some are short and others are long, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and in doing so lightly, do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you drill through it lightly, so that the nails go in at an angle so that they do not cut through the end of the bone, and must have a point or circle above it, so as not to let the point pass through the bone; and you will need more, so that each comes in at its own place in relation to the end of the bone, so that you have nails for all the test; and this is the shape of the three ways of making nails:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for drilling into bone is that you place the nail on top of the bone and twist it until you feel that the bone has been drilled through; then put the nail somewhere else a little apart, and so do all around, then cut off the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take out the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools that you have, such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if you see that you have left the ardour of the bone which is delayed by the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tenuous and more delicate than the other incisor; and if it does not remain nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, if the bone is lightly on the tools; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working which is that which Galen says, and it is more effective; and press it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens; so that when you have discovered this part, you shall place at its head the end of this lens-shaped incisor, from which it gets its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and is the part in two sides, so that the cutting is next to the bone; then proud of a small hammer above, so that you lightly hit the bone all around, and you give yourself well in guard of the membrane that is desoz; if it comes to the bone, so hit the bone lightly, for the bone well hurts without benefit, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break of the bone does not pierce just to the membrane, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then cover again that roughness, and shave the scales with a fine razor of which you must have different quantities, to administer in each one the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have before great razors, and after more subtle, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair treatments and fine incisions, you must bring the patient in accordance with their condition; and this is something that has not yet been answered by those who have studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the patient is unconscious, then you should wrap them in a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth, doubled over II or III times, and moisten it with wine and oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so as not to hurt the patient, and then tie it up, and do not remove it until the pustules have dried out a little; and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscesses have calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines in powder form, such as roots and flour of times and incense powder and aromatology and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer it again with medicine that does not sting; and guard against the wound becoming dirty, so you do not leave it to assemble bowels, for when bowels assemble over the silk of the skull, if they corrode and burn, they bring great harm to the patient; because when you put something sharp on the wound, it stings from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take heed, then, that no bad accident should come to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt. And if black dung only comes because of the medicine that has been put on, which has its virtue, let you take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix it with one cloth, and put it on the wound; then let you cure in a way that seems right to you until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the neck above are not broken by one blow, for they are two bones; and this bone is cartilage, and does not break unless it is pushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should pound your little finger or a part of the neck, and fit it back into its place with equal force at your index finger, and at the knuckle by turning, until the neck returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck, and can't get back to its place, if you believe that you should put it equal to the top of a small ray.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do this other way, and hurry to restore it the first day you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess has calmed down, then put a piece of linen cloth at the top of the neck where the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put another one from the other side if there is a break; and let the cloths be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that it must not be dried out; let each one be moistened every day.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is what is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, we must restore it according to one of the following two ways: which one is that you take a strong rod, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And you shall take two knots, and tie them together, and lift up the shoulder, and cut the sick person on a table; then lay the broken arm upon the fust, so that it comes to rest against the ground, and have a strong stick ready; then put the sick person's arm upon some heavy object or upon one of his ministers who holds it down; then make the doctor hold the shoulder equal to his hands together, until the broken part has returned as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other way is that the sick person should be made to rest upon his heel, and his hand should be tied to his neck; then order two of his ministers: one to hold what is on the broken part with his hands, and the other to tie fast all the limbs, and extend each to its place.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too much, then hold back the ligature from the rupture, and on the rupture, and extend each of the ministers to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the rupture is close to the shoulder blade, then you should put a ligature forward from the break, and another one on the side of the break; and also if the rupture is on the side of the neck, then you should put a light ligature without working too much, until the rupture is even on its place, and on its side; then you should make the rupture even, as it should be, and hold it back, so that the apostemes [bloody spots] don't come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the bloody spots come out, then don't hold back on extracting it for more than 7 days, and put a soft and oiled cloth on the rupture; then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put plaster on the rupture, then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the side; and wrap the bandage around, and extract it from the arm, so that the arm is in a natural position, unless something prevents it, or the bone is broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a lever, and put on the fracture one more wide and strong than the others, and leave between each lever two spaces, and let each be so large that it passes the fracture three times; then pull up on the levers, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the paste on the fracture, stronger and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the levers and the extraction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the member broken, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it be tied up until the seventh day, as we have said; then watch each three days whether the pus comes out or not to the place, so that the swelling does not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you follow our advice.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such accident occurs, if only it were not that the shoulder becomes loose after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, with his hands on his stomach; then set up the aid by wrapping it with a flat piece of wool, and check every hour during the day or night to see if the shape of the member is moving or if the ligaments are becoming softer; if so, treat it with medicine, and give him food as described earlier, in such a way that the food is at the first delicate level; and when he starts to improve, make it thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is usual for the aid and leg to be set again after forty days of everything; and then it must be dislocated and bath and medicines with ointments administered to set it right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if it is stiff and stuck, then it takes a day or two to loosen up.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small and one large; the small one is at the end of the elbow, and the large one is where the shoulder is attached; perhaps the large foscile breaks by itself, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is easy and quick, but when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more painful when it is broken by itself than when both are broken at the same time.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small foscile is broken, it is necessary to gently extend it and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Et s'il est grand, si le convient est de l'étirer plus fort; et l'étend sur un banc, et tienne le pouchet de la main plus haut que les autres, et les petits doigt plus bas que les autres doigt, et soit le malade croisé dessus lui même, et le banc devant lui plus haut, que le malade ne souffre nulle peine; puis étend les ministres sois bras à la partie désosée à sa main, ou à li liein, et un autre ministre à l'autre au desus.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is large, if it is convenient to stretch it more strongly; and extend it on a bench, and hold the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the bench in front of him higher, that the patient suffers no pain; then extend the ministers sois arms to the dislocated part at his hand, or to li liein, and another minister to the other above.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, let each one be put in its place, and if any of them have come loose and hold the two together, and you cannot restore it to its place, then mend it with wood and bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the caustic there is an injury, I have spoken of it to the peculiar chapter; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.
