And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, so I cover them with a caustic made of rosin oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and I cover them very gently, until the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then cover the bone with the cerates, and I put on the plaster of the powder from the mill with plenty of eggs, so that the splints are placed, and let the splint of the break be a little farther forward, and a little larger than the others; and know that there must be six splints or arms in several positions: whether the break is in one bone or in two; and stretch them more up than down, all the time keeping them moist and soft, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread with which they are stretched be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And keep the limb and the joint for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the member, as when it itches, let the member be soaked with warm water until the itch is gone; and do not restrict the member from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again to extract it, and if the joint is relaxed and the bone is exposed, and similar things, do not delay.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the joint can not be reset on the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it for a few days until the joint runs again, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not remove the sling until at least 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	I know that at the back of the hand and to us both happen little breaks, and comes but that a plier many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or plied, so that the patient is forced to cross, and sits straight in front of him evenly; then he puts his hand on a table spread out, and extends the broken bones, and sets them even the mirrours, as they are well joined; and puts the plaster and the stops, if an abscess comes, then I put a piece according to the quantity of the place; and is wrapped in a linen drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the backyard between the plant of the hand, so I make a piece of linen, and command the patient to strap his broken plant; and then I pull it out of a long drape, and is the piece of five-fold linen as big as the plant of the hand, and pulls it.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if his break is at the end, then it is necessary that you place a spike on, and another free in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then bind him tight around the hand, and seal the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if his break comes to either of the two, then it is necessary that you put a spike in, and another free at the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then bind him tight around the hand, and seal the ligature between the two; or you place a small right spike to raise the break and prevent it from moving; and if the break comes to the other two, as in the index or one of the others, then make it even, and tie it with the sound hand that is next to it; or you tie them all together, so that they do not move, or you put a spike on, as in the pouchet; and take care in the restoration and careful arrangement of the apothecary, and help him who comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the cold breeze
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The breath of the cold is often shaken, and we can see it when it turns before and behind; and restoration is such that we bind it above the shaker, and another cure.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his link equally to his side; and it is when the shaker has broken the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the shaking is near the root of the loins, so that one of the links toward the knuckle, and the other links away from the shaker.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the groin, and then are the links of the groin, and the extension below; then put the surgeon the bone equal with his two hands, as much as he is according to its natural figure, and then put the plaster, and bandage, because in the cutting there is no pain.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be calmed down, then return to your work and to your treatment; the time is right in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, wrap it in a bandage of tough leather twice over or three times over, and let the excess droop down; then return the leg to as much as possible to the root of the birth, and tie a long piece of thread between the thigh and the leg, freeing up the knee cap, and bring the end of the thread up; then return to the leg and to the thigh with the bandage, then put on stakes over the break, and put one stake over the bone in the leg; then fasten the leather between the leg and the thigh with sutures so that the tightening is even, then begin tying three or four times around the break; and as you go up the break, and lessening the tightening; then take the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie them together at the top, then return to the knee cap where you started, until you come to the roots; and if it does not move from its place, then let it be as it is, then if it comes no more swollen or deformed.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it falls, and addresses the one that comes to it, as we have often said; and if there are pieces of bone that hold it, if it can be done, so do it; and if not, split the place, and pull hard; and heal it as we have said, until he is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the kyide in this way as we have said, for the shoulder and arm; however, when restored in this way it does not cause the patient pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the kyide is healed on the second day, or a little more or less, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street from the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	And know that in the street from the knee there is little break, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, there is only a split or a dent, and all the pain comes out, and there is no pain, and this one feels better.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is so that one puts equal to him who is round on his two sides as long as he is united moves what one can; then put the plaster, and I put a flat stone if you need it, and hold it so as it should be, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other breakers, so that an abscess and another similar thing; so put to each accident what it comes to him as long as he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Sache that in the leg there are II bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all the breaks are like those of the arm; therefore the restoration is done equally, and all the work is done as well. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg returns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his thin nose is broken, turn him around.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick nose is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and turn it back.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then provide extension, and make it even, and bind the joints evenly; however, its break is ugly, and there are many pieces, so let the extension be smaller and lighter; and adjust it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two long hair strands that purple the leg on one side and another on the other, and they are as long as the leg from the ankle to the toe; then wrap them in two bands above and below, and bind the bandage firmly in the middle, and at this bandage no leg can decline towards the right or left, and so is good; and each day move each leg to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; if the cure until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but from the bones of the foot comes none at all and in several cases it has only been dislocated and not broken.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there should be a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones cross over each other, so that the person can barely stand on the ground, and as if he wanted to walk, then now put your foot on its side, where those bones are raised, then press it down until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and put it on, and tie the sole of the foot with a small flat piece of cloth, then fasten it around the ankle, and wrap up some bandages, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three days or four have passed, if the swelling has gone down, because you will find that the bones are even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s'il i a aucuns des deux brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as deux de la main; puis met au deux brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou deux, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j'ai dit, et l'estrain avenanment; et s'il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun deux une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sur lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu'il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things that I have said about other broken things, as we have said; and attend to each accident as it occurs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone down at the knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is broken in two at the knuckle, if the woman is seated in an enlarged position, then lean her back against the bed and support her from behind; then fill the opening of the nature with cotton, and put as much in as I can; then remove the woman from the bed, and gently pull on her back little by little, and at once let the cotton drop, until it enters the opening of the nature, and brings the bone with it; and when she urinates, if she holds the cotton back, and when she has urinated, let it be put back, and continue doing so for seven days or more: then will be restored the break, and there will no longer be pain, take a bladder of goat's milk, and tie a cord around the navel, and pour all of the milk into the opening; then blow into the cord forming, until the milk is gone inside: the opening will then be healed; then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days, until it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the man's or woman's jawbone is broken, return it to its place as we have said in the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts it into practice and use, and he hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means many things to do with the right way of restoration: hear then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and wrap it around; then cover with cloth, and leave for three days or more, and it will be healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fractures with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is appropriate for those who have fractures with wounds, even if they are great, such as the bones of the chest or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, so that the healed ones whom we have mentioned in our testimony may serve them.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the vitriol scorches, then you have nothing else, so start restoring the broken part in the same hour, or when the abscesses open.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses open, and you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the abscesses are calm, and do not touch them on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is protruding from the cheek, it is necessary that you put it out of joint slightly with your hand, with small movement.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands, take this instrument made of iron with seven or eight links long, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that he dip it in three or four times, according to what it needs in each cure of a broken part; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member at your work, and be sharp at the front and broad in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palainche," for it is convenient that the shoulder-blade be placed on the top of the chief of the bone; and is to be held thus at first, until it returns, and is even one with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, then you must strike at the top of the bone until the instrument has power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back in accordance with what we have said, using either an incision or a saw, within your power; then strike it with a tool of suitable size, or cut it from the bone with small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And if you make it so that it is in its place, then moisten the wound with black wine vinegar and properly tie it up; and do not put on wax or any other thing where there is oil, lest it cause pus and corruption; then administer leech salves when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times this has done the evil miraculously, and has brought upon the patient death or corruption in no case; and let the instrument be softer and more pliable than in other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it is not right to put it on splints; but wrap it in hard cloths instead of splints and bind it tight.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days break out boils on the wound, if there is anything that you have put on it that has come off, and bind it with a healing ointment, as with a four-fold tar and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be arranged so that the boils run down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes and it cannot be healed but comes together again, knowing that there are small pieces of bone causing it, you must cut the wound with a knife, and take out all these troublesome pieces that bring pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or another form of corruption, then you must heal it according to what the patient says about his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens up on the limb, as with the jaw or shoulder blade, or other large bones, do not pull it out, for many die, but leave it to rot; perhaps after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of bruces that come from the سودرة
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Come often do we come after the health of the برص (bruse), mostly when it is near a joint, and what an ugly thing it is to see the limb's form; and perhaps cannot make the member's movements natural.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, then, if we come to you with the برص (brus)  (brus), mostly when it is near a joint, and what an ugly thing it is to see the limb's form; and perhaps cannot make the member's movements natural. Do not apply any of these things separately, or all together, and confound them with wine, turpentine, myrrh, and sulfur, or the like, but put them on the lump in piles, and bind them well, and do not remove them for many days; and then loosen them, and start a new one, until the nodules are hard; or you tie them to a piece of string well made; for the property of the string is that it makes the swelling on the limbs hard; and if the nodule is already hard, it must be cut off, and the excess made visible; or you give it to a barber, until it is hard, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	two limbs which are weak after confinement
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and demure after weak and slender limbs for one of several reasons: because one is too tightly bound, and was not bound so as it should be; or because there are too many ligaments, and cannot come to the member's full extension; or because of too much inflammation; or because of too great movements, not in its hour; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body flexible, until the blood increases in it; and give him baths, and provide pleasure and rest; then put pitch on the member, so that the pitch attracts a lot of the full extension, and irrigate it often with hot water, until the full extension comes to the member; and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two members twisted after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the members are twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one should break a member all over again; many such fools have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm and even death result; however, if the nodules and tortures are fresh, they should be boiled in warm water or soft herbs are cooked, as foils of whale blubber, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the unguent should be made soft, such as well-made dye, and you take the musk of whale blubber, and confound it with goose fat or sisam oil, and make an unguent; or you take fig pastes, and grind them with hay of colon, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the arm placed so that it rubs continuously and repeatedly against moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make sure there is movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if it is twisted and stiffened, as in the case of stones, then it must be opened with a sharp knife lightly, and put ointment and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay it, and if by chance we put it back in place at its own pace; because then the joints do not move at all when brought to their original position: many times this causes pain and other pains; but when this has happened, so make sure to comfort the sick person, then let it rest, until the abscesses are calm; then raise the member with warm water and oil, then gently adjust it again, and cure each member as the cure comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the plasters for the dislocations of the shoulders until the tips.
des mandibules	of the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And I have ordered the plasters for dislocations of both jaws, and there are two ways for this: either they are slightly out of place and a little softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down to the neck, and the saliva flows from the mouth so that it cannot be held or the mouth closed, and envelops the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it by means of the following multiple positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entirely and completely dislocated, you must immediately bring it back to the hospital, and do not wait; and in such a way that the minister holding the head of the sick person, squeezes the mirrhe a little with one hand at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, the dislocation being of two parts; and the other two hands should be away, to make it even; and order the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he watches the wound heal evenly, until it regains its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And he brings the jaw back into place, most importantly, if both jaws are involved, then he warms them with hot water and oil, and brings them back slightly; do not delay in bringing them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is closed securely with a softener, then place it on sheets dipped in oil-and-wax cerot (a substance made of oil and wax), and gently tie them; let the patient sleep on his back, and have his chin between two pillows so that he does not move or strain himself, but eat leichtly, as long as the pains are gone and the jaws are healed; and then let him drink and eat leichtly, and do not work at opening the mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well-healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and sudden diseases come, and by chance abdominal discharge, and by chance vomit of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you know that it is a loss; and many times the one who has it dies, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not dislocate from the inside out along the course of the tooth, and is dislocated only once from one side to the other, and it is felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the sick person lies down on his back and stretches his arms; and then he presses the joint with his palm, and it will come back; then put the plaster and bandage on him, and bind it; and the jaw that is turned towards his throat cannot dislocate; unless so, and if it dislocates once, let him return to his place, as we have said; then put the plaster and bandage on, and bind it, and order the sick person to rest until he is well; and in this way the head of the shoulder is also reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	of shoulder dislocation
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And at times it happens to some men that the shoulder is broken or dislocated by a blow; and he thinks it has dislocated itself by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It therefore follows that you test it, as far as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And the dislocations are to be noted when they turn upwards towards the shoulder, and distinguish between the diseased and healthy shoulder, and you will find between them a clear difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and drive the top of the arm to the base of the neck, as if it were one body; and this type of dislocation cannot be brought back without difficulty, when it is new, or when the force has been applied to it while it was ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the ministers hold the hand of the sick person up, then put your fists on the shoulder, and hold the joint with force in place; and the ministers hold the hand, and raise it up, then put it out; so comes suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said above, in the hands of the ministers, then let the sick person be bathed in warm water; and administer a softening and soothing unguentation, as an infusion of aloes and fenugrec and melilote in water, and let it be applied; then let the sick person be sopped on his back, and put a sto of equal length behind the shoulder, not too soft nor too hard, and put the minister's heel on the sto, and hold the head of the shoulder properly, and draw the hand of the sick person up; and have other ministers turn the head of the sick person over, so that he does not move; this shoulder returns all at once, and stops if you do it according to this way: and it is that you do it as follows: let there be a man who is taller than the sick person; and stand on either side of his chest, and put the shoulder behind the shoulder of the sick person, and hold the joint in place, so that the sick person hangs down; and have other ministers draw the hand of the sick person down towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him put something heavy, and the dislocation will come back again.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And let them also do in another way: and is it that a long branch is stuck into the ground, whose head is also like a pistol, and is not too large or too small; then is put on the lou bad, but he has drapels water on, and the lou bad is lying down on the long stalk; then extend his hand downstream from another side forming, and the joint will come back to its place firmly; and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a branch of II arms of great and IIII fingers wide, which has the chief reont por mues enter em perfectly desoz the assele, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie sus the head of the stalk drapels water, that the stalk does not hurt the lou bad, then put it desoz the assele of the lou bad; and extend your arms up the stalk of the long branch, and lie the ajutoire on the stalk, and the arm at the chief of the hand, then put the arm on I escillon of a eschiele of large size, and let be estendue li hands downstream, and let be left li cors pendans d’autre part: the joint will come back now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is put in place, in whatever way, so that you put a sheep's wool rope equally, then put the plaster out of powder from the mill, with incense and canary of egg, on all the shoulder and back, then strain out the rope equally forward, and tie the bandage to the plaster, and embrace the hand at the neck, and let the hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he sucks a little, until the members are comfortable, because he will heal sooner; and then suck more after 5 or 7 days, and move them; and if they are firm and not softened, they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint moves out of its place due to moisture or another cause, so that you apply three torches, as it is put in front or plastered with torch.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it falls after seven days, and the joint does not stay, and he cannot raise his arm upstream, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint has never been properly placed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is caused by a fall backward, and the shoulders, or behind, is made by an impact, and stretching of the hands, and I will administer another place; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the recovery comes greasiness in the limb, and late movements, then the patient often bathes, until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation from the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint from the neck is dislocated in many places, and returns in many places; and it is dislocated from all sides, especially before and behind, and the dislocation is not properly replaced, for we see it and feel it well; and dislocate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the injured shoulder with the sound one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is worn out and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the shoulder joints do not come together, for if they come together, it would be worse to reset them; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all from the back, which is worse than other dislocations, and causes great pain, and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it is so far along that you can reset it, that you extend its hand with your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands are turned according to the shoulder inside, upside down and upside down, and press the joint into its root together, or at the base of its palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation up front, so it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and proud of the root of the palm let go which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, then give strong extension; and there are two who extend the arm, and they dye it from both sides so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm of each part, then you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when you see the joint to the joint of the hand, then oil it with any oil to soften the joint, then tighten the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, then put on dry plaster with honey of bee, and strain it firmly, and bind the arm to the throat of the patient, and leave it for some days, then let go.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is secure in its place, then loosen it and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, then start over with the plaster and the strapping and leave it like this for a few days, until it is securely fixed. Then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint has been moved, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is relieved; or put sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then work it, and let it enter or swim; and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the fat back on, and then enter or swim; and do this II or III times until he is well; and if you see that, put warm sheep's fat on the skin with butter, and strain it over; then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand is loose, and its return is lighter than that of other joints However, it must be brought back to place immediately while it is still displaced, so that the joint swells or there is a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the setting-back so that you put the ill-hand on a tray, and spread the fingers of the hand, and make it equal so that its palm is placed on the appearance of the joint, and hold it like that until it comes back However, it is necessary for you to check if it is well placed; then put the back of the hand of the patient on a tray while you extend and set it back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the patient's back hand on the tray, and place his hand on its appearance.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then this is good; but if it is extracted from the pustules that relax the abscesses, and he leaves it thus unremedied.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If it cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint is twisted; and there is no help for the patient except to cut the nerve or artery, unless there is another device than to extract by a delicate cauterizing of the case, and perhaps there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have spoken of, then extract and leave it for 5 days, then remove it and leave it again.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then soak it in hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not dislocated at either end, nor on the back of the palm or the abdomen; then they are brought together and the dislocation is pushed down to the knuckles until it heals, and then the tip of the finger is bent towards the part where it is joined, and left there for a day, and then made straight again that day; and then let it rest, as we have said, and then move it again, and then make it straight, and do this often enough so that it doesn't hurt, and also do this if it is dislocated in the abdomen of the hand, and do the same as you did before until it is well; and do the same if it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the wrist on the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or the jaw is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there will be no cure unless you return them to their place, for otherwise the patient will die quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the exudations spring forth without volition, nor can they be retained, and often a limb is softened, or the II ribs or the II arms or I And often the eschinee moves III parts; that which moves behind is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you should treat it if the gilbositez comes from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing of all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting down or striking or similar things, the ancient methods of cure with great words brought little benefit to all; but I have condensed it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre formant, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nous avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sur l'épine formant, tant qu'il revienne.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Et s'elle ne revient par ceste cure, si prenne une taule de III bras de lonc, et cheve desoz la paroit, et li maleide soit en coste, et boute le chief de la taule desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la taule sus l'espinette; et mette li mires ses piez sur l'autre chief de la taule, et presse bien, tant qu'il revienne au leu; et si tu veux, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not respond to this cure, then take a table three arms long, and shave one side of it, and let the patient lie on his side, and pour the water from the table over his head, then put the middle of the table over the spine; and set the minister's fingers on the other end of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do the same with the turner that turns in your hand. And then tie the link that is among the helpers to the turner toward the head, and the other link to the turner toward the fingers, and let each minister turn his turner on all the link, and the master put the spine in order as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, put it on with dry plaster and then the daps, and then the wooden tablet of III long feet, which purplishly marks the place of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then the thread of a rope, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle fasting until he is well; and if at the end of health anything comes, then administer medicines that soften and even it out, with the tablet that we have mentioned above; and never give him a piece of lead, and never come to appearance in the back spine of the back, and be careful that this is dislocations; and that is the bone that opens, for which one should not have presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the joints of the hip and the shoulder come only from dislocations, not at all like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parties: inside and outside, before and behind; and more inside there, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy, it is longer, and more so than the healthy genitals, and the sick cannot double his knee on fire; and it is the place which is swollen hot by an abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that one who comes to the outside, is that this accident is opposite to these in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that one who comes in front are that his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, it does not double the knee with pain, and if one makes him walk, he cannot go before, and holds back his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has been behind, if it is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder of the hip is out of place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And the signs of this dislocation if it is that you ignore it, then it lingers according to its disposition, so there is no cure; and it is not worth taking a chance.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, so hurry that you reset the joint, and turn it in and out, and move it to the left and right; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not come back in this way, then it is necessary that you prepare one minister very well, and hold the leg very firmly with two hands, or tie it to the floor with a strong rope; and other ministers extend their hand above and below at the same time, so that they press their hands against his arms, then tie him to the rope under the armpit; and others pull back his head; and they extend both sides simultaneously, so that the patient is raised from the ground once, and stays like that.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put cure on its appearance When the dislocations are in the head, you must lay the patient down on his back, then place the bandage over the crown of the head, and the cloth that is removed from the angle, then put the bandage upwards towards the angle, and upwards towards the forceps; then take other ministers to its arms, and embrace the large cloth of the diseased cuixe, and extend it towards the end form: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is more lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot put it in this way that we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two legs of the sick together with a strong bandage wrapped around the heels and knees, and let the sick leg be extended twice as much as the other one; then hang it by the head from a post, and let its two arms be outstretched; then command a minister who will embrace the head of the cuixe, and let there be other ministers hanging with the sick one, who will embrace the cuixe well, for the joints now return very well.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	Et when the dislocations are in the way, so lie down the patient, as we have said before in that which has gimbosity, and extrude him by the foot properly, and also by the leg; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then put one torch between the legs of the patient against the form; and plant there drapes moistened around, lest they hurt the patient, then spread each servant towards him, and let the doctor set the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a table, and press him as we have said in gimbosity, and lie down the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, so extend the injured leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and let the doctor place his pain on the injured ankle, then press with the other hand, and extend it sideways towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are far away, it is not convenient to extend the patient downward, nor to lift him up from the ground, but rather that he should be as if he were lying on his back as we have said in the case of two legs; and on his face, and the strap extended as we have said before, and you should press it on the joint to the table; and it will be complete when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; so then set the splint, and put the plaster, and strain it with a bandage, so that the leg does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then remove it, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, then strain them again, as before, and let them rest for three days; then remove them, and let them go, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the hip
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	is displaced within and without, and behind; but does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if it does not bend at the hip, so that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee between your palms, and pull apart with both hands, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and other ministers extend his foot, until the hip returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg at the hip easily; and put the plaster on, and make him walk, and join the members together firmly for three days or four. Then let him loose; and do not work the patient to walk, until the members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, give a strong extension, as we said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation at the heel
